على إذن القاضي. ويخالفه ما في الخانية في هنا كلام الشرنبلالية . قوله : (بأن يتملكها) قال في النهر : معنى الانتفاع بها صرفها إلى نفسه كما في الفتح. وهذا لا يتحقق ما بقيت في يده لا تملكها كما توهمه في البحر لما أنها باقية على ملك صاحبها ما لم يتصرف فيها حتى لو كانت أقل من نصاب وعنده ما تصير به نصاباً حال عليه الحول تحت يده كالأجنبي المسألتين فإنه قال لو أراد الملتقط أن يصرفها إلى نفسه بعدما عرفها هذه المدة فهو على وجهين : إن كان الملتقط غنياً لا يجوز له الانتفاع عندنا سواء فعل ذلك بأمر القاضي أو بغير أمره، وإن كان الملتقط فقيراً إن أذن له القاضي أن ينفقها على نفسه يحل له أن ينفق ولا يحل بغير أمر القاضي عند عامة العلماء. وقال بشر : يحل .اهـ. وإنما فسرنا الانتفاع بالتملك لأنه ليس المراد الانتفاع بدونه كالإباحة ولذا ملك بيعها وصرف الثمن إلى نفسه كما في الخانية . أطلق في عدم الانتفاع للغني فشمل القرض ولذا قال في فتح القدير : وليس للملتقط إذا كان غنياً أن يتملكها بطريق القرض إلا بإذن الإمام، وإن كان فقيراً فله أن يصرفها إلى نفسه صدقة لا قرضاً اهـ. وأطلق في ولده فشمل الصغير والحاصل أن أقارب الملتقط وأصوله وفروعه لأن الجواز للفقر وهو موجود في الكل وينبغي تقييد الصغير بأن يكون وزوجته الملتقط فقيراً لأن الولد يعد غنياً بغناء أبيه كما قدمناه في الزكاة ولم يذكر المصنف حكم ما إذا انتفع بها الملتقط ثم حضر المالك لأنه معلوم من حكم ما إذا تصدق بها الملتقط ثم حضر المالك بالأولى فله أن يجيز وأن يضمن. وفي الخانية: رجل وجد عرضاً لقطة فعرفها ولم يجد صاحبها وهو فقير ثم أنفق على نفسه ثم أصاب مالاً قالوا: لا يجب عليه أن يتصدق على الفقراء بمثل ما أنفق على نفسه - زاد في الولوالجية - وهو المختار فأفاد الاختلاف. وفي الخانية : امرأة وضعت ملاءتها وجاءت امرأة أخرى ووضعت ملاءتها ثم جاءت الأولى وأخذت ملاءة الثانية وذهبت لا ينبغي للثانية أن تنتفع بملاءة الأولى لأنه انتفاع بملك الغير، فإن أرادت أن تنتفع بها قالوا ينبغي أن تتصدق هي بهذه الملاءة على ابنتها إن كانت فقيرة على نية أن يكون ثواب الصدقة لصاحبتها إن رضيت ثم تهب الابنة الملاءة منها فيسعها الانتفاع بها لأنها بمنزلة اللقطة فكان سبيلها التصدق، وإن كانت غنية لا يحل لها الانتفاع بها، وكذلك الجواب في المكعب إذا سرق منه . وقيده بعضهم بأن يكون المكعب الثاني مثل الأول أو أجود، أما إذا كان الثاني دون الأول فله أن ينتفع به من غير هذا التكلف لأن أخذ الأجود وترك الأدون دليل الرضا بالانتفاع بالأدون ؛ كذا في الظهيرية. وفيه مخالفة اللقطة من جهة لا يجب عليه زكاة اهـ. ومقتضاه أنها لو كانت عيناً فانتفع بها بلبس ونحوه لا يملكها مع أنه يصدق عليه أنه صرفها إلى نفسه ومراد المؤلف بالتملك الاحتراز عن الإباحة كما ينبه عليه أي ينتفع بها ملكه حال الانتفاع لا أنه يباح له الانتفاع بها باقية على ملك صاحبها وإلا لم يكن له بيعها وهي فليتأمل. قوله : وظاهر كلامهم متوناً وشروحاً (الخ يخالفه ما في متن مواهب الرحمن : وينتفع بها بإذن القاضي، وقيل بدونه وعزا الأول في شرحه البرهان إلى الأكثر كما نقله عنه في الشرنبلالية . قوله : (وينبغي تقييد الصغير بأن يكون الملتقط فقيراً) قال في النهر : هذا سهو بل المراد الكبير إذ المسألة ما إذا كان الملتقط غنياً وله ابن فقير وهذا لا يتأتى في الصغير فكيف يشمله
His statement: (And he benefits from it if he is poor, otherwise he gives charity to a stranger and to his parents, wife, and child if they are poor) i.e., the finder benefits from the luqata by owning it, on condition that he is poor, considering both sides, just as it is permissible to give it to another poor person. As for the rich person, he is not allowed to benefit from it. If it is someone other than the finder, it is apparent from the hadith: 'If its owner does not come, then give it in charity.' And charity is only given to the poor like obligatory charity, and if it is the finder himself, it is the same. Imam al-Shafi'i said: It is permissible because of his ﷺ saying in the hadith of Abu (may Allah be pleased with him): 'If its owner comes, give it to him; otherwise benefit from it, and he was among the rich.' And because it is only permitted for the poor to encourage him to pick it up for its preservation, and the rich share in that. Our proof is: It is the property of another, so benefiting from it is not permitted except with his consent, due to the general texts. Permission for the poor is based on what we narrated, or by consensus, so what remains is on the original principle. The rich person is considered as taking it due to the possibility that he may become poor during the period of announcement, while the poor person may become negligent due to the possibility that he may become rich during that time. The benefit taken by Abu (رضي الله عنه) was with the permission of the Imam, and it is permissible with his permission as in al-Hidayah. Thus, it conveys that a rich person may benefit with the Imam's permission, but on the basis of a loan, as restricted by al-Zayla'i and others. The apparent meaning of their words in the texts and commentaries is that the permissibility for the poor after the announcement does not depend on the permission of the qadi. This is contradicted by what is in al-Khaniyyah... (marginal note). His statement: (by owning it) He said in al-Nahr: The meaning of benefiting from it is spending it on himself, as in al-Fath. This is not realized as long as it remains in his hand without ownership, as misunderstood in al-Bahr, because it remains the property of its owner until he disposes of it. Even if it is less than the nisab and he has what makes it a nisab, the year passes while it is in his hand, like a stranger... He said: If the finder wants to spend it on himself after having announced for this period, there are two aspects: If the finder is rich, he is not allowed to benefit from it according to us, whether he does so by the order of the qadi or without. If the finder is poor, if the qadi permits him to spend it on himself, it is permissible for him to spend, and it is not permissible without the qadi's order according to the general body of scholars. Bishr said: It is permissible. End. And we interpreted benefiting as owning, because the intent is not benefiting without that, like mere permissibility, hence he is allowed to sell it and spend its price on himself as in al-Khaniyyah. He issued an absolute prohibition for the rich, which includes a loan, so it was said in Fath al-Qadir: A rich finder cannot own it by way of a loan except with the Imam's permission; if poor, he may spend it on himself as charity, not as a loan. End. And he made absolute regarding his child, including the minor. The summary is that the relatives of the finder, his ancestors and descendants, because the permissibility is for poverty, and it exists in all. It should be restricted that the minor must be such that the finder himself is poor, because a child is considered rich if his father is rich, as we presented in Zakat. The author did not mention the ruling if the finder benefits from it and then the owner appears, because it is known from the ruling if the finder gives it in charity and then the owner appears, a fortiori: he has the option to confirm or to hold liable. In al-Khaniyyah: A man found an item as luqata, announced it, did not find the owner, and he was poor, then he spent it on himself, then he acquired wealth. They said: He is not obligated to give in charity to the poor an amount equivalent to what he spent on himself. Al-Walwajiyyah added: This is the preferred view, indicating difference. In al-Khaniyyah: A woman placed her cloak and another woman placed her cloak, then the first came and took the second's cloak and left. It is not proper for the second to benefit from the first's cloak because it is benefiting from another's property. If she wants to benefit from it, they said she should give this cloak in charity to her daughter if she is poor, intending that the reward of the charity be for its owner if she is pleased; then the daughter gifts the cloak to her; then it becomes permissible for her to benefit because it is like the luqata, so its course is charity. If she is rich, it is not permissible for her to benefit from it. Similarly, the answer in the case of a cube (muka'ab) if stolen from him. Some restricted it to the second cube being like the first or better; if the second is inferior to the first, he may benefit without this complexity because taking the better and leaving the inferior indicates consent to benefit from the inferior. Thus in al-Zahirah. And in it there is a difference from luqata in that zakat is not obligatory on him. End. Its implication is that if it were an 'ayn (property) and he benefited by wearing etc., he does not own it, even though it is true that he spent it on himself. The author's intent by 'ownership' is to exclude mere permissibility, as he alerts: he benefits from it as his own at the time of benefiting, not that it is permissible for him to benefit while it remains the property of its owner; otherwise he would not be able to sell it, so reflect. His statement: And apparent from their words in texts and commentaries... contradicts what is in the text of Mawahib al-Rahman: He benefits with the permission of the qadi, and it is said without, and the first is attributed to the majority in its commentary al-Burhan, as quoted from him in al-Shurnublaliyyah. His statement: (It should be restricted that the minor be such that the finder is poor) He said in al-Nahr: This is a slip; rather the intended is the adult, because the issue is when the finder is rich and has a poor son, and this does not apply to a minor, so how could it include him.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling on the finder's (multaqit) use of the found item (luqata) after the period of announcement. The key principle: If the finder is poor, he may benefit from the luqata by owning it and spending it on himself. If he is rich, he must give it in charity to the poor. This applies both to giving to a stranger and to his own needy relatives (parents, wife, child). The passage includes a significant inter-madhhab dispute: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that even a rich finder may benefit from the luqata, based on the hadith of Abu (رضي الله عنه) where the Prophet said '...otherwise, benefit from it, and he was among the rich.' The Hanafi response is that the luqata is someone else's property, and permission to use it without the owner's consent is exceptional; the hadith is interpreted as allowing only for the poor, or as requiring the owner's consent. The hadith of Abu is further explained: his use was with the permission of the Imam (ruler), which is allowed as a loan (qard) for the rich. For the poor, the majority of Hanafi scholars (including the matn and shuruh) hold that the qadi's permission is not required; however, some (as in al-Khaniyyah and Mawahib al-Rahman) require the qadi's permission. The text also clarifies that 'benefiting' means ownership and the ability to sell it and spend the proceeds; it is not mere permissibility to use while it remains the owner's property. A special case: if the finder later becomes rich, he is not obligated to repay the equivalent. This is the preferred view (al-mukhtar). The passage then presents a related scenario: a woman's cloak swapped mistakenly, similar to luqata. The solution involves giving it in charity to one's daughter, then taking it as a gift. This is permissible only if the recipient is poor. Finally, there is a correction regarding the child of a rich finder: if the finder is rich and his son is poor, the finder cannot give the luqata to his son because the son is considered rich through his father's wealth; the intended is the adult child (or the father if the finder is poor).

Key Terms
الانتفاع (al-intifa'): Using the luqata for personal benefit, either by consuming it or owning it.
الفقير (al-faqir): A person who does not own property equal to his needs; the finder must be poor to benefit from luqata.
إذن الإمام (idhn al-imam): Permission from the ruler or qadi to use the luqata; some scholars require this even for the poor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, what is required for a poor finder to benefit from the luqata after the announcement period?
A) He must obtain permission from the qadi.
B) He may benefit without any permission.
C) He must first give it in charity and then reclaim it.
D) He must wait one more year.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a poor finder to own the luqata after announcement without qadi permission, but a rich finder must give it in charity, based on the hadith commanding charity and the principle of owner's consent.

Ruling on Taking a Runaway Slave: Conditions and Dispute
Ruling on taking a runaway slave: conditions and dispute about obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking a runaway slave, identify the conditions that change the ruling, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute about whether it becomes obligatory when loss is feared.

Core Idea
Taking a runaway slave is recommended, not obligatory, except when loss is imminent and one has full ability, according to some Hanafi scholars.

This lesson examines the ruling on taking a runaway slave (abaq). The matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq states that it is 'liked' (mustahab) but conditional on the ability to secure the slave. The commentator explains the reasoning: returning the slave revives the property rights of the master. However, a dispute arises among Hanafi scholars: does the ruling shift to obligation when the slave is likely to be lost? This analysis traces the proofs and the intra-madhhab debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Read the matn phrase 'أخذه أحب أن يقوم عليه' (Taking him, it is liked that he be able). The word 'أحب' indicates mustahab (recommended). The ruling is thus istihbab, not obligation.
The base ruling is conditional on ability (يقوم عليه).
2
Understand the condition of ability
The commentator restricts the recommendation to when one is able to take the slave. If unable, there is no recommendation. This is a shart (condition) for the ruling.
Ability includes physical and practical capacity to secure the slave.
3
Examine the analogy to lost property (luqata)
The author of al-Bada'i' equates the ruling of taking a runaway slave to that of taking lost property. This analogy is the basis for the dispute: in luqata, taking is not fard even when loss is feared; so here too, it should not be fard.
The analogy (qiyas) is the key proof structure.
4
Analyze the dispute: does fear of loss impose obligation?
Some Hanafis (al-Bada'i', al-Fath) argue that if one fears the slave will be lost (e.g., death or theft), and one has full ability, taking becomes fard. Other Hanafis (al-Nahr) reject this, insisting the analogy to luqata does not permit obligation.
Al-Nahr calls the contrary view a 'gross error' (غلط فاحش).
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon Hanafi view is that taking remains mustahab in general. However, some later authorities allow obligation if there is strong likelihood of loss and full ability. The final ruling is nuanced.
For practical fatwa, the majority view (mustahab) is preferred, but the stricter view is noted for precaution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أخذه أحب أن يقوم عليه) أي يقدر عليه لما فيه من إحيائه لأنه هالك في حق المولى فيكون الرد إحياء له. قيد بقدرته على أخذه لأنه لو لم يقدر فلا استحباب، ولم يذكر ما إذا خاف هلاكه لو لم يأخذه. وصرح في البدائع بأن حكم أخذه حكم أخذ اللقطة فعلى هذا يفترض أخذه إن خاف ضياعه، ويندب إن لم يخف، ويحرم أخذه لنفسه، ويستحب تركه إن لم يأمن على نفسه. ولم يذكر المصنف كثيراً من أحكامه في البدائع : إن شاء الآخذ أمسكه حتى يجيء صاحبه، وإن أخذه قال بعد كتاب الإباق قوله : (فعلى هذا يفترض أخذه إن خاف ضياعه الخ قال في النهر : هذا غلط فاحش وذلك أنه قدم عن البدائع أن أخذ اللقطة مع خوف الضياع ليس بفرض وأن القول بالفرضية مذهب الشافعي فكيف يفهم من قوله أن حكم أخذه حكم أخذ اللقطة أنه يكون فرضاً فسبحان من تنزه عن السهو والنسيان نعم في الفتح يمكن أنه يجري فيه التفصيل في اللقطة بين أن يغلب على ظنه تلفه على المولى إن لم يأخذه مع قدرة تامة عليه فيجب أخذه وإلا فلا
His saying: 'Taking him, it is liked that he be able to take him' means he is able to take him, because in it is reviving him, as he is dead in the right of the master, so returning him is a revival. He restricted it with his ability to take him because if he is not able, there is no recommendation. He did not mention the case when he fears his destruction if he does not take him. And he stated explicitly in al-Bada'i that the ruling of taking him is like the ruling of taking lost property. So on this basis, taking him becomes obligatory if he fears his loss, and recommended if he does not fear, and forbidden to take him for himself, and preferred to leave him if he does not trust himself. And the author did not mention many of his rulings in al-Bada'i: if the taker wishes, he keeps him until his owner comes, and if he takes him he said... after Kitab al-Ibaq his saying: 'On this basis, taking him becomes obligatory if he fears his loss etc.' He said in al-Nahr: This is a gross error. He presented from al-Bada'i that taking lost property with fear of loss is not obligatory, and that the statement of obligation is the school of al-Shafi'i. So how can it be understood from his saying that the ruling of taking him is like the ruling of taking lost property that it would be obligatory? Glory be to the One who is free from forgetfulness and mistake. Yes, in al-Fath it is possible that the detail in lost property applies: if he strongly thinks it will be lost to the owner if he does not take it while having full ability, then it becomes obligatory to take it, otherwise not.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn line from Kanz al-Daqaiq: 'Taking him, it is liked that he be able to take him.' The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) explains that 'its being liked' (istihbab) is conditional on the ability to take the runaway slave. The reason for recommendation is that returning the slave revives him from the perspective of the master, as the slave is considered 'dead' in terms of benefit to the owner. The commentator notes that al-Bada'i' states the ruling of taking a runaway is the same as taking lost property (luqata). According to al-Bada'i', if one fears the slave will be lost (e.g., if left, he may die or be stolen), then taking becomes obligatory (farḍ). If no fear, it is recommended (mandūb). Taking for one's own use is ḥarām. Leaving him is recommended if one does not trust oneself. However, a dispute arises: the commentator al-Nahr criticizes the author of al-Bada'i' for implying that taking becomes obligatory when fearing loss, arguing that in the case of lost property, the ruling is not obligatory even with fear of loss; the view of obligation is Shafi'i, not Hanafi. The commentator then softens this by noting that in al-Fath, there is a detail: if one strongly believes the owner will lose the slave if not taken, and one has full ability, then it becomes obligatory; otherwise not. This intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf centers on whether the analogy with luqata extends to obligation.

Key Terms
آبق (abaq): A slave who runs away with the intention of hiding from his master.
استحباب (istihbab): A ruling that the act is recommended but not obligatory; its omission is not sinful.
لقطة (luqata): Lost property picked up by a finder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Nahr, the author of the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq, what is the correct Hanafi view on taking a runaway slave when there is fear of loss?
A) It becomes fard (obligatory) because of the fear of loss
B) It remains mustahab (recommended) because the analogy to lost property does not support obligation
C) It becomes haram because taking without permission is theft
D) It becomes makruh because of potential harm to the finder

Key Takeaway
Taking a runaway slave is recommended (mustahab) when able, but a minority of Hanafis make it obligatory when loss is feared; the relied-upon view is mustahab.

Reward for Returning a Runaway Slave
Ruling on the reward (jaʿl) for returning a runaway slave from a journey's distance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jaʿl for returning a runaway slave, explain the proof from Companion practice, and identify the exceptions (lost animals, free children, household members) where no reward is given.

Core Idea
Forty dirhams for a journey's return; no reward for lost animals or free children.

This lesson unpacks a key Hanafi ruling on the reward (jaʿl) for returning a runaway slave. The rule is not based on a contract but on istihsan, grounded in the unanimous practice of the Companions. We'll explore the fixed amount, the condition of a journey's distance, and important exceptions that every student of fiqh must know.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
First, note that the reward of forty dirhams is wajib by istihsan, not by a prior agreement. The proof is the Companions' practice (ijmaʿ).
Istihsan is a Hanafi principle that allows departure from qiyas for a stronger reason.
2
Understand the fixed amount
The amount is fixed at forty dirhams for a journey (approx. 48 miles), and proportionally less for shorter distances. This is a compromise among varying Companion opinions.
Some Companions set forty, others less; the Hanafi school chose forty for the full journey.
3
Distinguish the runaway slave from a lost animal
The text explains that no reward is given for returning a lost animal (dall) because it does not intentionally hide and the owner can find it by tracks. The finder should leave it, not take it.
The same distinction applies to imprisonment: a runaway is imprisoned to prevent re-flight; a lost animal is not.
4
Recognize when no reward is given
No reward is given for returning a free child. Also, exceptions include someone who is already in the master's household (e.g., a servant), the parents, or the son (if not in the master's care).
The text is cut off but lists further exceptions. Two people sharing the forty if they both return the slave is also discussed.
5
Apply the ruling
In a hypothetical case, if a stranger returns a runaway from a journey's distance, the master must pay forty dirhams. If the master denies the slave ran away, the master's word is taken, but if proof is brought, the reward is due.
This shows the evidentiary aspect: the returner may need to prove the slave was a runaway.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ومن رده من مدة سفر فله أربعون درهما جعلاً له استحساناً يستحقها على مولاه بلا شرط لأن الصحابة رضي الله عنهم اتفقوا على أصل وجوب الجعل إلا أن منهم من جعله أربعين ومنهم من أوجب دونه فأوجب الأربعين في مسيرة السفر وما دونها فيما دونه توفيقاً وتلفيقاً، فلو جاء بالآبق رجل فأنكر مولاه إباقه فالقول له، فإن برهن أنه أبق أو أن مولاه أقر بذلك قبلت؛ كذا في الجوهرة قيد بالآبق لأنه لا جعل لراد الضال لأنه بالسمع ولا سمع في الضال فامتنع ولأن الحاجة إلى صيانة الضال دونها في الآبق لأنه لا يتوارى والآبق يختفي، وهذا مما فارق فيه الآبق وكذا في حبسه فإن الآبق إذا رفع إلى الإمام يحبسه ولا يحبس الضال لأنه لا يؤمن على الآبق من الإباق ثانياً بخلاف الضال، وكذا لا يأخذه الواجد بل تركه أفضل على أحد القولين لأنه لا يبرح من مكانه فيجده المالك بخلاف الآبق، وكذا لا جعل لراد الصبي الحر. أطلق الراد فشمل ما إذا كانا اثنين فيشتركان في الأربعين إذا رداه لمولاه كما في الحاوي. وشمل ما إذا رده محرمه إليه فهو كالأجنبي لكن يرد عليه ما إذا رده من في عيال سيده إليه فإنه لا جعل له وكذا يرد عليه ما إذا رده الأبوان أو أحدهما ولم يكن في عياله لا جعل له وكذا يرد عليه لو رده الابن إلى أبيه وليس في عياله أو أحد
His saying: 'And whoever returns him from a journey's duration has forty dirhams as a reward for him, by istihsan, he deserves it from the master without condition, because the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, agreed upon the principle of the necessity of the reward, except that some of them made it forty and some made it less. So he made forty obligatory for the distance of a journey, and less for less, as a compromise and combination. So if a man brings the runaway and his master denies his running away, the statement is the master's. If he proves that he ran away or that the master admitted to that, it is accepted; as in al-Jawharah. He restricted it to the runaway, because there is no reward for the returner of the lost animal (dall), because it is by hearing, and there is no hearing in the lost animal, so it is prevented. And because the need to safeguard the lost animal is less than in the runaway, because it does not hide, while the runaway hides. And this is one of the ways the runaway differs. Likewise in his imprisonment: if the runaway is brought to the imam, he imprisons him, but he does not imprison the lost animal, because one is not safe from the runaway running away again, unlike the lost animal. Likewise, the finder should not take it; rather leaving it is better according to one of the two opinions, because it does not leave its place, so the owner will find it, unlike the runaway. Likewise, there is no reward for the returner of a free child. He used the word 'returner' generally, so it includes if there are two, then they share the forty if they return him to his master, as in al-Hawi. And it includes if a mahram returns him to him, he is like a stranger. But there is an exception: if someone who is in the care of the master returns him, he has no reward. Likewise, there is an exception: if the parents or one of them return him, and he is not in their care, there is no reward. Likewise, there is an exception: if the son returns him to his father, and he is not in his care, or one...
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn: 'And whoever returns him from a journey's duration has forty dirhams.' The ruling is established by istihsan (juristic preference), based on the practice of the Companions (ijma'). They agreed that a reward (ja'l) is due for returning a runaway slave, but differed on the amount; the Hanafi school sets it at forty dirhams for a journey's distance, and less for shorter distances. The reward is owed by the master unconditionally (i.e., without a prior contract). The commentator then distinguishes between a runaway slave and a lost animal (dall): there is no reward for returning a lost animal because the animal does not have the intent to flee, and the owner can find it by following its tracks. Also, a runaway slave is imprisoned by the imam to prevent further flight, but a lost animal is not imprisoned. Similarly, the finder of a lost animal should not take it but leave it, unlike a runaway where taking is recommended. No reward is given for returning a free child. The passage also discusses cases where multiple people return the slave: they share the forty dirhams. If a mahram (unmarriageable relative) returns him, he is like a stranger and gets the reward. However, exceptions are made for those already in the master's household (e.g., a servant) and for parents or children who return the slave, if they are not in the master's care—they do not get the reward. The latter part is cut off but continues with the exception.

Key Terms
جعل (ja'l): A fixed reward given to someone who returns a runaway slave to his master, based on the practice of the Companions.
ضال (dall): A lost domestic animal or person who has no intention to hide; the owner may still find it by following tracks.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is NOT entitled to the reward for returning a runaway slave?
A) A stranger who returns the slave from a journey's distance
B) A mahram relative of the master
C) The master's servant who returns the slave
D) Two people who together return the slave

Key Takeaway
The reward for returning a runaway slave is a fixed forty dirhams for a journey's distance, wajib by istihsan, with clear exceptions for lost animals, free children, and household members.

The Reward (Ja'l) for Returning a Runaway Slave: Ruling and Proof
Ruling statement with proof and comparison

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of forty dirhams for the returner of a runaway slave from a travel distance and explain its evidential basis in ijma and istihsan.

Core Idea
The Companions agreed on a reward; Hanafis set 40 dirhams for a journey by istihsan.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq expounds the ruling on the ja'l (reward) for returning a runaway slave. The Hanafi school relies on istihsan, departing from strict analogy, and on the consensus of the Companions. The text also distinguishes this case from lost property and a free child.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is returning a runaway slave from a travel distance. The ruling is that the returner gets forty dirhams as a reward (ja'l).
The reward is a set amount, not based on negotiation.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites the consensus of the Companions as the proof. The Sahaba agreed on the obligation of a reward, though they differed on the amount. The Hanafis take the maximum (40 dirhams) for the full travel distance and adjust for shorter distances.
Ijma is a primary source; the ruling is further supported by istihsan.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Companions' agreement establishes the principle; the Hanafis then apply istihsan to fix the amount, combining the different reports as a compromise.
This is not strict qiyas; istihsan overrides the analogy to lost property.
4
Note the distinction from lost property and free child
The text explicitly states that there is no reward for returning a lost animal or a free child. The reason is that the need is less (the animal does not hide) and the duty is not established by revelation.
The distinction highlights the specificity of the runaway slave ruling.
5
Note the unconditional nature
The reward is given without any prior condition or agreement. The returner does not need to have asked for a reward; it is enforced on the master.
This is a point of contrast with other forms of reward (ju'alah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإباق دبره شاء ذهب به إلى صاحبه، فإن ادعى إنسان أنه عبده وبرهن دفعه إليه واستوثق بكفيل إن شاء لجواز أن يدعيه آخر، وإن لم يبرهن وأقر العبد لمدعيه دفعه إليه أيضاً لعدم المنازع ويأخذ كفيلاً، فإن طالت المدة باعه القاضي وحفظ ثمنه لصاحبه، فإن جاء صاحبه بعده وبرهن دفع الثمن إليه وليس له نقض البيع لأن بيع القاضي بولاية شرعية، ولو زعم المدعي أنه وكاتبه لم يصدق في نقض البيع اهـ. وسيأتي حكم نفقته آخراً ويستحلف القاضي مدعيه مع البرهان بالله أنه باقٍ إلى الآن في ملكك لم يخرج ببيع ولا هبة كما في فتح القدير. وفي الظهيرية : ينبغي للراد أن يأتي به إلى الإمام عند السرخسي وخيره الحلواني، وإذا جاء به إلى القاضي هل يصدقه القاضي بلا بينة؟ اختلف المشايخ فيه كما اختلفوا في نصب القاضي خصماً لمدعيه حتى تقبل بينته ولم يذكره محمد كما اختلفوا في أخذ الكفيل من مدعيه بعد البرهان كما اختلفوا في أخذ الضال، وإذا أبق العبد وذهب بمال المولى فجاء به رجل وقال لم شيئاً فالقول قوله ولا شيء عليه، ولا يكون وصول يده إلى العبد دليلاً على وصول أجد معه يده إلى المالية اهـ .
قوله: (ومن رده من مدة سفر فله أربعون درهما جعلاً له استحساناً يستحقها على مولاه بلا شرط لأن الصحابة رضي الله عنهم اتفقوا على أصل وجوب الجعل إلا أن منهم من جعله أربعين ومنهم من أوجب دونه فأوجب الأربعين في مسيرة السفر وما دونها فيما دونه توفيقاً وتلفيقاً، فلو جاء بالآبق رجل فأنكر مولاه إباقه فالقول له، فإن برهن أنه أبق أو أن مولاه أقر بذلك قبلت؛ كذا في الجوهرة قيد بالآبق لأنه لا جعل لراد الضال لأنه بالسمع ولا سمع في الضال فامتنع ولأن الحاجة إلى صيانة الضال دونها في الآبق لأنه لا يتوارى والآبق يختفي، وهذا مما فارق فيه الآبق وكذا في حبسه فإن الآبق إذا رفع إلى الإمام يحبسه ولا يحبس الضال لأنه لا يؤمن على الآبق من الإباق ثانياً بخلاف الضال، وكذا لا يأخذه الواجد بل تركه أفضل على أحد القولين لأنه لا يبرح من مكانه فيجده المالك بخلاف الآبق، وكذا لا جعل لراد الصبي الحر. أطلق الراد فشمل ما إذا كانا اثنين فيشتركان في الأربعين إذا رداه لمولاه كما في الحاوي. وشمل ما إذا رده محرمه إليه فهو كالأجنبي لكن يرد عليه ما إذا رده من في عيال سيده إليه فإنه لا جعل له وكذا يرد عليه ما إذا رده الأبوان أو أحدهما لو كان مالكه قد استعاذ به كما لو قال لرجل إن عبدي أبق فإذا وجدته فخذه كما في فتح القدير وشرط في التتارخانية أن يقول له نعم معللاً بأنه وعد له الإعانة وكذا يرد عليه لو رده السلطان أو الشحنة أو الخفير الأجر بالعمل وكذا العبد إلا أن الجعل لمولاه لأنه ليس من أهل ملك المال؛ كذا في البدائع. وشمل ما إذا رده بنفسه أو نائبه. قال في المحيط : أخذ آبقاً من مسيرة سفر فدفعه إلى رجل وأمره أن يأتي به إلى مولاه وأن يأخذ منه الجعل جاز. وذكر في آخر الباب لو أخذ عبداً آبقاً فاغتصبه منه رجل وجاء به لمولاه فدفعه إليه وأخذ جعله ثم جاء الذي أخذه فأقام البينة أنه أخذه من مسيرة ثلاثة أيام فإنه يأخذ من مولاه الجعل ثانياً على الغاصب بما دفع إليه لأنه أخذه بغير حق .اهـ. وأطلق في السيد فشمل البالغ والصبي فيجعل الجعل في ماله وشمل ما إذا كان متعدداً فالجعل على قدر النصيب، فلو كان البعض غائباً فليس للحاضر أن يأخذه حتى يعطي تمام الجعل، ولا يكون متبرعاً. بنصيب الغائب فيرجع عليه. وأطلق في المردود فشمل ما إذا كان صغيراً فهو كالكبير؛ ذكره الحاكم في الكافي لكن ذكر بعده : وإذا أبقت الأمة ولها صبي رضيع فردهما رجل كان له جعل واحد، فإن كان ابنها غلاماً قد قارب الحلم فله الجعل ثمانون درهماً .اهـ. وقيد ولد الآبقة بالمراهق ولم يرجع المولى غاية البيان ومعراج الدراية وفتح القدير والعناية والبزازية والقهستاني والنهر أن الأب كبقية المحارم إن كان في عياله لا جعل له وإلا فله الجعل وعبارة المعراج : والجملة في ذلك أن الراد إذا كان في عيال مالك العبد أي في مؤنته ونفقته لا جعل له سواء كان الراد أباً للمالك أو ابناً له، وأما إذا لم يكن في عياله فعلى التفصيل، إن كان الراد ابن المالك فلا جعل له أيضاً وإن كان أباه فله الجعل. إليه أشار في الذخيرة وشرح الطحاوي وفي المبسوط : جواب القياس أن الراد ذا الرحم المحرم يستحق الجعل في جميع ذلك إذا لم يكن في عياله ولكنه استحسن فقال : إذا وجد الابن عبد أبيه فلأجعل له منه ، سواء كان في عياله أو لا، لأن رده على أبيه من جملة خدمته وخدمة الأب مستحقة على الابن، أما لو كان الراد أباً فإن كان في عيال ابنه لا جعل له لأن أبق الرجل إنما يطلبه من في عياله عادة ولهذا ينفق عليهم فلا يستوجب مع جعل آخر، وإن لم يكن الأب في عياله فله الجعل لأن خدمة الابن غير مستحقة على الأب اهـ . ثم رأيت في الحاوي القدسي ما نصه : وإذا كان الراد ممن في عيال مالك الغلام لا جعل له، وإن لم يكن في عياله فله الجعل، سواء كان أجنبياً أو ذا رحم محرم إلا الوالدين والمولودين اهـ. فتأمل. قوله : (وشرط في التتارخانية أن يقول له نعم) قال المقدسي : الظاهر أنه ليس بشرط لأن الظاهر منه التبرع بالعمل حيث لم يشرط عليه جعلاً. قوله :
Book of Runaway Slaves... [detailed rulings on returning]. (From the text): He said: "And whoever returns him from a journey's distance, he gets forty dirhams as a reward (ja'l) for him by istihsan, which he deserves from his master without any condition, because the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, agreed on the principle of the obligation of the reward, except that some of them made it forty and some obligated less, so they obligated forty for the distance of a journey and less for what is less, as a compromise. So if a man brings the runaway and his master denies his running away, the statement is his; if he proves that he ran away or that his master admitted that, it is accepted. Likewise in al-Jawhara: it is restricted to the runaway because there is no reward for returning a lost animal because it is by hearing and there is no hearing in a lost animal, so it is prevented, and because the need to protect the lost animal is less than in the runaway, because it does not disappear and the runaway hides, and this is how the runaway differs. Likewise in his imprisonment: if the runaway is brought to the imam, he imprisons him, but he does not imprison the lost animal because the runaway is not safe from running away a second time, unlike the lost animal. Likewise, the finder should not take it; rather, leaving it is better according to one of the two opinions, because it does not leave its place, so the owner will find it, unlike the runaway. Likewise, there is no reward for returning a free child. He gave an absolute statement for the returner, so it includes if there are two, so they share the forty if they return him to his master, as in al-Hawi. And it includes if a mahram returns him to him, so he is like a stranger, but it is objected if someone who is in the master's household returns him to him, then he has no reward. Likewise, it is objected if the parents or one of them returns him and he is not in his household, then he has no reward. Likewise, it is objected if the son returns him to his father and he is not in his household, or one of the spouses to the other. Likewise, it is objected if the guardian returns him to the orphan, and likewise whoever supports the orphan if he returns him after he ran away and he is not a guardian. Likewise, it is objected if his owner had asked him to take it, as if he said to a man: 'My slave ran away, so if you find him, take him,' as in Fath al-Qadir, and in al-Tatarkhaniyya he stipulated that he should say 'yes', reasoned that he promised him assistance. Likewise, it is objected if the sultan or the police or the guard returns him, because the action is obligatory upon them. So the list is eleven. So if it is said: if the returner guards the master's property or serves him or asks for his help, it is safe from the objection, as is not hidden. And it includes whether the returner is an adult or a child, free or slave, because the child is among those who deserve wages for work, and likewise the slave, except that the reward is for his master because he is not among those who own property; as in al-Bada'i. And it includes if he returns him himself or his deputy. In al-Muhit: He took a runaway from a journey's distance and gave him to a man and ordered him to bring him to his master and take the reward from him, it is permissible. And at the end of the chapter, if a man took a runaway slave and another man forcibly took him from him and brought him to his master and gave him to him and took his reward, then the one who took him came and established evidence that he took him from a distance of three days, then he takes the reward from the master a second time from the usurper for what he paid, because he took him without right. He gave absolute for the master, so it includes the adult and the child, so the reward is made from his wealth. And it includes if there are multiple, so the reward is according to the share. So if some are absent, the present one may not take it until he gives the full reward, and he is not a volunteer for the absent one's share, so he returns to him. He gave absolute for the returned, so it includes if he is small, so he is like the big one; al-Hakim mentioned it in al-Kafi, but he mentioned after it: If a female slave runs away and she has a suckling child, and a man returns them both, he gets one reward. But if her son is a boy near puberty, then he gets eighty dirhams. He restricted the child of the female runaway to the adolescent. And the master does not return... Ghayat al-Bayan, Mi'raj al-Diraya, Fath al-Qadir, al-Inaya, al-Bazzaziyya, al-Qahistani, and al-Nahr state that the father is like the rest of the maharim: if he is in his household, he has no reward; otherwise, he has the reward. The expression of al-Mi'raj: The summary is that the returner, if he is in the household of the slave's owner, i.e., in his maintenance and expenses, he has no reward, whether the returner is the father of the owner or his son. But if he is not in his household, then with detail: if the returner is the son of the owner, he also has no reward; if he is his father, he has the reward. This is referred to in al-Dhakhira and Sharh al-Tahawi. In al-Mabsut: The answer of analogy is that the returner who is a mahram relative deserves the reward in all that if he is not in his household, but he (the author) used istihsan and said: If the son finds his father's slave, he has no reward from him, whether he is in his household or not, because returning him to his father is part of his service, and service of the father is obligatory upon the son. But if the returner is the father, then if he is in his son's household, he has no reward, because the runaway is usually sought by those in his household, and therefore he spends on them, so he does not deserve another reward. And if the father is not in his son's household, he has the reward, because service of the son is not obligatory upon the father. Then I saw in al-Hawi al-Qudsi its text: If the returner is among those in the household of the owner of the boy, he has no reward; if he is not in his household, he has the reward, whether he is a stranger or a mahram relative, except for the parents and children. So reflect. His statement: (And in al-Tatarkhaniyya he stipulated that he should say 'yes') al-Maqdisi said: Apparently it is not a condition, because the apparent is that he is volunteering the work since he did not stipulate a reward on him. His statement:
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the ruling on the reward (ja'l) for returning a runaway slave (abaq). The Hanafi school establishes, based on istihsan (juristic preference), that whoever returns a slave who has run away from a distance of travel (masirat safar, typically three days' journey) is entitled to a fixed reward of forty dirhams from the master, without any prior agreement. This is because the Companions agreed in principle that there should be a reward, though they differed on the amount; the Hanafis reconcile the reports by setting forty dirhams for a travel distance and less for shorter distances. The text then distinguishes the runaway slave from lost property (dalal): no reward is given for returning a lost animal because the need is less and it usually stays in place, while a runaway intentionally hides. The passage enumerates numerous exceptions where no reward is given, primarily when the returner is financially dependent on the master (fi 'iyalihi) or when the returner is a son returning his father's slave (since serving the father is the son's duty). The father, however, if not in his son's household, does get the reward. Other exceptions include the owner himself, one who was asked to take the slave, the sultan or police (since it's their duty), and cases where the returner is a slave (the reward goes to his master). The text also covers the scenario of two returners sharing the reward, the case of a female slave with a child, and the ruling if the reward is taken by a usurper. Finally, it discusses a condition from al-Tatarkhaniyya that if the owner said 'take him' and the returner said 'yes', this constitutes a promise of assistance; al-Maqdisi argues that such a statement is not a condition for entitlement.

Key Terms
جعل (ja'l): A fixed reward or compensation given to the returner of a runaway slave, set at 40 dirhams for a travel distance.
آبق (abaq): A slave who has run away from his master.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used to depart from strict qiyas in favor of a ruling that is more equitable or based on specific evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the basis for the forty dirham reward for returning a runaway slave from a travel distance?
A) General qiyas (analogy)
B) Istihsan and Ijma of the Companions
C) A hadith from the Prophet
D) Analog to lost property

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes a fixed reward of forty dirhams for returning a runaway slave from a travel distance, based on the consensus of the Companions and juristic preference (istihsan).

Exceptions and Special Cases in the Ja'l for Returning a Runaway Slave
List of exceptions with detailed rulings and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the eleven exceptions where no ja'l is given and apply the special rules for relatives, multiple returners, and the condition of assent.

Core Idea
No reward when the returner is duty-bound or financially dependent on the master.

This passage continues the exposition of the ja'l, detailing numerous exceptions. The text enumerates eleven cases where no reward is due, including when the returner is in the master's household, a son returning his father's slave, or an official acting out of duty. It also discusses the intra-Hanafi difference on whether verbal assent is required.

Guided Path
1
List the eleven exceptions from the text
Go through the text and enumerate each case where the returner does not get the ja'l. These are: 1) someone in the master's household, 2) parents (if in the household), 3) son returning father's slave, 4) one spouse to the other, 5) guardian returning to orphan, 6) caretaker of orphan (non-guardian), 7) the owner asking someone (who says 'yes'), 8) sultan, 9) police (shuhna), 10) guard (khafir), 11) others? Actually text lists 11 total.
The text says 'الفاردة إحدى عشرة' indicating eleven items.
2
Identify the common rationale
The common thread is that these returners are either duty-bound to act (official duties, filial duty) or financially dependent on the master (household members). The reward is not given because they would be expected to return the slave without extra compensation.
This rationale is not explicitly stated but inferred from the cases.
3
Analyze the father/son dispute
There is an intra-Hanafi disagreement. According to al-Mabsut, the son never gets the reward (even if independent), while the father gets the reward if not in the son's household. This is based on istihsan: the son's service to the father is obligatory, so returning the slave is part of that duty.
Al-Hawi al-Qudsi adds that the exception is only for parents and children, not other maharim.
4
Discuss the condition of saying 'yes'
The text mentions a stipulation from al-Tatarkhaniyya that if the owner asks someone to fetch the runaway and the person says 'yes', that constitutes a promise of assistance, so no reward. But al-Maqdisi disagrees, saying the apparent is that the person is volunteering work, so the condition is not required.
The relied-upon view is that saying 'yes' is not a condition for the reward.
5
Apply to special cases: multiple returners, child, slave, nursing mother
If two people return the slave together, they share the 40 dirhams. If a child or slave returns the slave, the reward still applies (though the slave's reward goes to his master). If a female slave with a child is returned, one reward is given, but if the child is near puberty, two rewards (80 dirhams) are due.
These details show the comprehensive nature of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإباق دبره شاء ذهب به إلى صاحبه، فإن ادعى إنسان أنه عبده وبرهن دفعه إليه واستوثق بكفيل إن شاء لجواز أن يدعيه آخر، وإن لم يبرهن وأقر العبد لمدعيه دفعه إليه أيضاً لعدم المنازع ويأخذ كفيلاً، فإن طالت المدة باعه القاضي وحفظ ثمنه لصاحبه، فإن جاء صاحبه بعده وبرهن دفع الثمن إليه وليس له نقض البيع لأن بيع القاضي بولاية شرعية، ولو زعم المدعي أنه وكاتبه لم يصدق في نقض البيع اهـ. وسيأتي حكم نفقته آخراً ويستحلف القاضي مدعيه مع البرهان بالله أنه باقٍ إلى الآن في ملكك لم يخرج ببيع ولا هبة كما في فتح القدير. وفي الظهيرية : ينبغي للراد أن يأتي به إلى الإمام عند السرخسي وخيره الحلواني، وإذا جاء به إلى القاضي هل يصدقه القاضي بلا بينة؟ اختلف المشايخ فيه كما اختلفوا في نصب القاضي خصماً لمدعيه حتى تقبل بينته ولم يذكره محمد كما اختلفوا في أخذ الكفيل من مدعيه بعد البرهان كما اختلفوا في أخذ الضال، وإذا أبق العبد وذهب بمال المولى فجاء به رجل وقال لم شيئاً فالقول قوله ولا شيء عليه، ولا يكون وصول يده إلى العبد دليلاً على وصول أجد معه يده إلى المالية اهـ .
قوله: (ومن رده من مدة سفر فله أربعون درهما جعلاً له استحساناً يستحقها على مولاه بلا شرط لأن الصحابة رضي الله عنهم اتفقوا على أصل وجوب الجعل إلا أن منهم من جعله أربعين ومنهم من أوجب دونه فأوجب الأربعين في مسيرة السفر وما دونها فيما دونه توفيقاً وتلفيقاً، فلو جاء بالآبق رجل فأنكر مولاه إباقه فالقول له، فإن برهن أنه أبق أو أن مولاه أقر بذلك قبلت؛ كذا في الجوهرة قيد بالآبق لأنه لا جعل لراد الضال لأنه بالسمع ولا سمع في الضال فامتنع ولأن الحاجة إلى صيانة الضال دونها في الآبق لأنه لا يتوارى والآبق يختفي، وهذا مما فارق فيه الآبق وكذا في حبسه فإن الآبق إذا رفع إلى الإمام يحبسه ولا يحبس الضال لأنه لا يؤمن على الآبق من الإباق ثانياً بخلاف الضال، وكذا لا يأخذه الواجد بل تركه أفضل على أحد القولين لأنه لا يبرح من مكانه فيجده المالك بخلاف الآبق، وكذا لا جعل لراد الصبي الحر. أطلق الراد فشمل ما إذا كانا اثنين فيشتركان في الأربعين إذا رداه لمولاه كما في الحاوي. وشمل ما إذا رده محرمه إليه فهو كالأجنبي لكن يرد عليه ما إذا رده من في عيال سيده إليه فإنه لا جعل له وكذا يرد عليه ما إذا رده الأبوان أو أحدهما ولم يكن في عياله لا جعل له وكذا يرد عليه لو رده الابن إلى أبيه وليس في عياله أو أحد الزوجين إلى الآخر، وكذا يرد عليه لو رده الوصي إلى اليتيم وكذا من يعول اليتيم إذا رد قد ابقه وليس بوصي، وكذا يرد عليه لو كان مالكه قد استعاذ به كما لو قال لرجل إن عبدي أبق فإذا وجدته فخذه كما في فتح القدير وشرط في التتارخانية أن يقول له نعم معللاً بأنه وعد له الإعانة وكذا يرد عليه لو رده السلطان أو الشحنة أو الخفير لوجوب الفعل عليهم فالوارد إحدى عشرة فلو قال إذا كان الراد يحفظ مال السيد أو يخدمه أو استعان به لسلم من الإيراد كما لا يخفى. وشمل ما إذا كان الراد بالغاً أو صبياً حراً أو عبداً لأن الصبي من أهل استحقاق الأجر بالعمل وكذا العبد إلا أن الجعل لمولاه لأنه ليس من أهل ملك المال؛ كذا في البدائع. وشمل ما إذا رده بنفسه أو نائبه. قال في المحيط : أخذ آبقاً من مسيرة سفر فدفعه إلى رجل وأمره أن يأتي به إلى مولاه وأن يأخذ منه الجعل جاز. وذكر في آخر الباب لو أخذ عبداً آبقاً فاغتصبه منه رجل وجاء به لمولاه فدفعه إليه وأخذ جعله ثم جاء الذي أخذه فأقام البينة أنه أخذه من مسيرة ثلاثة أيام فإنه يأخذ من مولاه الجعل ثانياً على الغاصب بما دفع إليه لأنه أخذه بغير حق .اهـ. وأطلق في السيد فشمل البالغ والصبي فيجعل الجعل في ماله وشمل ما إذا كان متعدداً فالجعل على قدر النصيب، فلو كان البعض غائباً فليس للحاضر أن يأخذه حتى يعطي تمام الجعل، ولا يكون متبرعاً. بنصيب الغائب فيرجع عليه. وأطلق في المردود فشمل ما إذا كان صغيراً فهو كالكبير؛ ذكره الحاكم في الكافي لكن ذكر بعده : وإذا أبقت الأمة ولها صبي رضيع فردهما رجل كان له جعل واحد، فإن كان ابنها غلاماً قد قارب الحلم فله الجعل ثمانون درهماً .اهـ. وقيد ولد الآبقة بالمراهق ولم يرجع المولى غاية البيان ومعراج الدراية وفتح القدير والعناية والبزازية والقهستاني والنهر أن الأب كبقية المحارم إن كان في عياله لا جعل له وإلا فله الجعل وعبارة المعراج : والجملة في ذلك أن الراد إذا كان في عيال مالك العبد أي في مؤنته ونفقته لا جعل له سواء كان الراد أباً للمالك أو ابناً له، وأما إذا لم يكن في عياله فعلى التفصيل، إن كان الراد ابن المالك فلا جعل له أيضاً وإن كان أباه فله الجعل. إليه أشار في الذخيرة وشرح الطحاوي وفي المبسوط : جواب القياس أن الراد ذا الرحم المحرم يستحق الجعل في جميع ذلك إذا لم يكن في عياله ولكنه استحسن فقال : إذا وجد الابن عبد أبيه فلأجعل له منه ، سواء كان في عياله أو لا، لأن رده على أبيه من جملة خدمته وخدمة الأب مستحقة على الابن، أما لو كان الراد أباً فإن كان في عيال ابنه لا جعل له لأن أبق الرجل إنما يطلبه من في عياله عادة ولهذا ينفق عليهم فلا يستوجب مع جعل آخر، وإن لم يكن الأب في عياله فله الجعل لأن خدمة الابن غير مستحقة على الأب اهـ . ثم رأيت في الحاوي القدسي ما نصه : وإذا كان الراد ممن في عيال مالك الغلام لا جعل له، وإن لم يكن في عياله فله الجعل، سواء كان أجنبياً أو ذا رحم محرم إلا الوالدين والمولودين اهـ. فتأمل. قوله : (وشرط في التتارخانية أن يقول له نعم) قال المقدسي : الظاهر أنه ليس بشرط لأن الظاهر منه التبرع بالعمل حيث لم يشرط عليه جعلاً. قوله :
Book of Runaway Slaves... [detailed rulings on returning]. (From the text): He said: "And whoever returns him from a journey's distance, he gets forty dirhams as a reward (ja'l) for him by istihsan, which he deserves from his master without any condition, because the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, agreed on the principle of the obligation of the reward, except that some of them made it forty and some obligated less, so they obligated forty for the distance of a journey and less for what is less, as a compromise. So if a man brings the runaway and his master denies his running away, the statement is his; if he proves that he ran away or that his master admitted that, it is accepted. Likewise in al-Jawhara: it is restricted to the runaway because there is no reward for returning a lost animal because it is by hearing and there is no hearing in a lost animal, so it is prevented, and because the need to protect the lost animal is less than in the runaway, because it does not disappear and the runaway hides, and this is how the runaway differs. Likewise in his imprisonment: if the runaway is brought to the imam, he imprisons him, but he does not imprison the lost animal because the runaway is not safe from running away a second time, unlike the lost animal. Likewise, the finder should not take it; rather, leaving it is better according to one of the two opinions, because it does not leave its place, so the owner will find it, unlike the runaway. Likewise, there is no reward for returning a free child. He gave an absolute statement for the returner, so it includes if there are two, so they share the forty if they return him to his master, as in al-Hawi. And it includes if a mahram returns him to him, so he is like a stranger, but it is objected if someone who is in the master's household returns him to him, then he has no reward. Likewise, it is objected if the parents or one of them returns him and he is not in his household, then he has no reward. Likewise, it is objected if the son returns him to his father and he is not in his household, or one of the spouses to the other. Likewise, it is objected if the guardian returns him to the orphan, and likewise whoever supports the orphan if he returns him after he ran away and he is not a guardian. Likewise, it is objected if his owner had asked him to take it, as if he said to a man: 'My slave ran away, so if you find him, take him,' as in Fath al-Qadir, and in al-Tatarkhaniyya he stipulated that he should say 'yes', reasoned that he promised him assistance. Likewise, it is objected if the sultan or the police or the guard returns him, because the action is obligatory upon them. So the list is eleven. So if it is said: if the returner guards the master's property or serves him or asks for his help, it is safe from the objection, as is not hidden. And it includes whether the returner is an adult or a child, free or slave, because the child is among those who deserve wages for work, and likewise the slave, except that the reward is for his master because he is not among those who own property; as in al-Bada'i. And it includes if he returns him himself or his deputy. In al-Muhit: He took a runaway from a journey's distance and gave him to a man and ordered him to bring him to his master and take the reward from him, it is permissible. And at the end of the chapter, if a man took a runaway slave and another man forcibly took him from him and brought him to his master and gave him to him and took his reward, then the one who took him came and established evidence that he took him from a distance of three days, then he takes the reward from the master a second time from the usurper for what he paid, because he took him without right. He gave absolute for the master, so it includes the adult and the child, so the reward is made from his wealth. And it includes if there are multiple, so the reward is according to the share. So if some are absent, the present one may not take it until he gives the full reward, and he is not a volunteer for the absent one's share, so he returns to him. He gave absolute for the returned, so it includes if he is small, so he is like the big one; al-Hakim mentioned it in al-Kafi, but he mentioned after it: If a female slave runs away and she has a suckling child, and a man returns them both, he gets one reward. But if her son is a boy near puberty, then he gets eighty dirhams. He restricted the child of the female runaway to the adolescent. And the master does not return... Ghayat al-Bayan, Mi'raj al-Diraya, Fath al-Qadir, al-Inaya, al-Bazzaziyya, al-Qahistani, and al-Nahr state that the father is like the rest of the maharim: if he is in his household, he has no reward; otherwise, he has the reward. The expression of al-Mi'raj: The summary is that the returner, if he is in the household of the slave's owner, i.e., in his maintenance and expenses, he has no reward, whether the returner is the father of the owner or his son. But if he is not in his household, then with detail: if the returner is the son of the owner, he also has no reward; if he is his father, he has the reward. This is referred to in al-Dhakhira and Sharh al-Tahawi. In al-Mabsut: The answer of analogy is that the returner who is a mahram relative deserves the reward in all that if he is not in his household, but he (the author) used istihsan and said: If the son finds his father's slave, he has no reward from him, whether he is in his household or not, because returning him to his father is part of his service, and service of the father is obligatory upon the son. But if the returner is the father, then if he is in his son's household, he has no reward, because the runaway is usually sought by those in his household, and therefore he spends on them, so he does not deserve another reward. And if the father is not in his son's household, he has the reward, because service of the son is not obligatory upon the father. Then I saw in al-Hawi al-Qudsi its text: If the returner is among those in the household of the owner of the boy, he has no reward; if he is not in his household, he has the reward, whether he is a stranger or a mahram relative, except for the parents and children. So reflect. His statement: (And in al-Tatarkhaniyya he stipulated that he should say 'yes') al-Maqdisi said: Apparently it is not a condition, because the apparent is that he is volunteering the work since he did not stipulate a reward on him. His statement:
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the ruling on the reward (ja'l) for returning a runaway slave (abaq). The Hanafi school establishes, based on istihsan (juristic preference), that whoever returns a slave who has run away from a distance of travel (masirat safar, typically three days' journey) is entitled to a fixed reward of forty dirhams from the master, without any prior agreement. This is because the Companions agreed in principle that there should be a reward, though they differed on the amount; the Hanafis reconcile the reports by setting forty dirhams for a travel distance and less for shorter distances. The text then distinguishes the runaway slave from lost property (dalal): no reward is given for returning a lost animal because the need is less and it usually stays in place, while a runaway intentionally hides. The passage enumerates numerous exceptions where no reward is given, primarily when the returner is financially dependent on the master (fi 'iyalihi) or when the returner is a son returning his father's slave (since serving the father is the son's duty). The father, however, if not in his son's household, does get the reward. Other exceptions include the owner himself, one who was asked to take the slave, the sultan or police (since it's their duty), and cases where the returner is a slave (the reward goes to his master). The text also covers the scenario of two returners sharing the reward, the case of a female slave with a child, and the ruling if the reward is taken by a usurper. Finally, it discusses a condition from al-Tatarkhaniyya that if the owner said 'take him' and the returner said 'yes', this constitutes a promise of assistance; al-Maqdisi argues that such a statement is not a condition for entitlement.

Key Terms
عيال (iyal): Household; those financially dependent on the master.
جعل (ja'l): A fixed reward or compensation given to the returner of a runaway slave, set at 40 dirhams for a travel distance.
آبق (abaq): A slave who has run away from his master.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used to depart from strict qiyas in favor of a ruling that is more equitable or based on specific evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following returners does NOT get the ja'l for returning a runaway slave?
A) The master's father if he is financially independent
B) The master's son if he is financially independent
C) A stranger who returns the runaway from a travel distance
D) The master's brother if he is not in the household

Key Takeaway
The ja'l for returning a runaway slave is not given when the returner is under a duty to act or is financially dependent on the master, with specific rules for relatives.

Reward for Returning Runaway: Father vs Son
Ruling with proof on reward for father and son returners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reward for returning a runaway slave when the returner is the owner's father or son, and explain the role of istihsan in overriding qiyas.

Core Idea
A son never gets reward for returning his father's slave, even if not in maintenance, because filial service is obligatory.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into the nuances of the reward for returning a runaway slave. While the general rule grants reward to any returner not under the owner's maintenance, an exception is made for the son of the owner due to his duty to serve his father. The father, however, is treated like other mahram relatives—he gets the reward if not dependent on his son.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The default ruling (qiyas) is that any returner not in the owner's maintenance deserves the reward. This applies to all mahram relatives, including father and son, unless an exception is established.
2
Recognize the exception for the son
Despite qiyas, the son gets no reward even if not in maintenance. The reason (illa) is that returning the father's slave is part of his obligatory service to his father. This exception is based on istihsan (juristic preference), as recorded from Imam Muhammad.
Istihsan overrides qiyas due to the stronger evidence of filial duty.
3
Distinguish the father's case
The father is not obliged to serve his son. Therefore, if the father is not in his son's maintenance, he gets the reward. If he is in the son's maintenance, he is already supported and thus entitled to no additional reward.
4
Understand the role of maintenance
Being in the owner's maintenance (fi 'iyalihi) negates reward for any returner, because the returner is already compensated through support. This is a separate condition from the relationship.
Maintenance is a secondary factor; for the son, the primary bar is filial duty.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a returner who is the owner's son: no reward ever. Given a returner who is the owner's father: reward only if not in the son's maintenance. Apply the rule to any case by checking (a) relationship and (b) maintenance status.
The ruling is definitive in the Hanafi school (mufta bihi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويرجع المولى غاية البيان ومعراج الدراية وفتح القدير والعناية والبزازية والقهستاني والنهر أن الأب كبقية المحارم إن كان في عياله لا جعل له وإلا فله الجعل وعبارة المعراج : والجملة في ذلك أن الراد إذا كان في عيال مالك العبد أي في مؤنته ونفقته لا جعل له سواء كان الراد أباً للمالك أو ابناً له، وأما إذا لم يكن في عياله فعلى التفصيل، إن كان الراد ابن المالك فلا جعل له أيضاً وإن كان أباه فله الجعل. إليه أشار في الذخيرة وشرح الطحاوي وفي المبسوط : جواب القياس أن الراد ذا الرحم المحرم يستحق الجعل في جميع ذلك إذا لم يكن في عياله ولكنه استحسن فقال : إذا وجد الابن عبد أبيه فلأجعل له منه ، سواء كان في عياله أو لا، لأن رده على أبيه من جملة خدمته وخدمة الأب مستحقة على الابن، أما لو كان الراد أباً فإن كان في عيال ابنه لا جعل له لأن أبق الرجل إنما يطلبه من في عياله عادة ولهذا ينفق عليهم فلا يستوجب مع جعل آخر، وإن لم يكن الأب في عياله فله الجعل لأن خدمة الابن غير مستحقة على الأب اهـ . ثم رأيت في الحاوي القدسي ما نصه : وإذا كان الراد ممن في عيال مالك الغلام لا جعل له، وإن لم يكن في عياله فله الجعل، سواء كان أجنبياً أو ذا رحم محرم إلا الوالدين والمولودين اهـ. فتأمل. قوله : (وشرط في التتارخانية أن يقول له نعم) قال المقدسي : الظاهر أنه ليس بشرط لأن الظاهر منه التبرع بالعمل حيث لم يشرط عليه جعلاً. قوله :
And the master refers to Ghayat al-Bayan, Miraj al-Diraya, Fath al-Qadir, al-Inaya, al-Bazzaziyya, al-Qahistani, and al-Nahr that the father is like the rest of the mahram relatives; if he is in his maintenance, no reward for him, otherwise he has the reward. And the expression of al-Miraj: the summary in that is that the returner, if he is in the maintenance of the owner of the slave, i.e., in his support and expenditure, no reward for him, whether the returner is the owner's father or son. But if he is not in his maintenance, then in detail: if the returner is the owner's son, then no reward for him either; if he is his father, then he has the reward. This is indicated in al-Dhakhira and Sharh al-Tahawi, and in al-Mabsut: the answer of analogy (qiyas) is that the returner who is a mahram relative deserves the reward in all that if he is not in his maintenance, but he (Imam Muhammad) exercised istihsan and said: if the son finds his father's slave, he has no reward from him, whether he is in his maintenance or not, because returning it to his father is part of his service, and the father's service is obligatory upon the son. As for if the returner is a father, if he is in his son's maintenance, no reward for him, because the runaway of the man is only sought by those in his maintenance usually, and for this he spends on them, so he does not deserve another reward; if the father is not in his son's maintenance, he has the reward because the son's service is not obligatory upon the father. End. End. So reflect. Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses the specific ruling when the returner of the runaway slave is a close relative (father or son) of the owner. The key distinction is whether the relative is under the owner's maintenance (fi 'iyalihi). The consensus from multiple works (Ghayat al-Bayan, Miraj al-Diraya, etc.) is that if the returner is in the owner's maintenance, no reward is due, regardless of the relationship. If not in his maintenance, then: if the returner is the owner's son, he still does not get the reward because serving the father is part of his filial duty; if the returner is the owner's father, he gets the reward because the son is not obliged to serve the father in this specific manner. Al-Mabsut explains the basis: qiyas would grant the reward to any mahram relative not in the maintenance, but istihsan denies it to the son due to the obligation of paternal service. The passage also references al-Hawi al-Qudsi which generally denies reward to parents and children (i.e., the owner's parents and children) if they are in his maintenance, but allows it otherwise. Finally, it notes a condition from al-Tatarkhaniyya that the returner must verbally agree to the owner's request, but al-Maqdisi argues this is not a condition as the returner's action indicates volunteerism unless a reward was stipulated.

Key Terms
المحارم (al-mahārim): Close blood relatives with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, such as parents, children, siblings, etc.
عيال (ʿiyāl): Those under one's maintenance and support, i.e., dependents.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that allows departing from qiyas for a stronger reason, here the son's obligation to serve his father.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a father get the reward for returning his son's runaway slave?
A) Always, regardless of maintenance
B) Never, because he is a relative
C) Only if he is not in his son's maintenance
D) Only if he is in his son's maintenance

Key Takeaway
The son's obligation to serve his father overrides the general entitlement to reward, while the father retains his entitlement unless dependent.

The Eleven Categories Entitled to Reward for Returning a Runaway Slave
Enumeration of eleven categories of returners and the basic rule of entitlement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eleven categories of returners entitled to the reward for returning a runaway slave and identify the one exception where the reward is not due.

Core Idea
Eleven categories of people are entitled to the reward for returning a runaway slave, unless they are under the owner's maintenance or obligated by duty.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq opens the chapter on runaway slaves by enumerating the specific individuals who qualify for the reward (ju'l) when they return a runaway. The list includes spouses, guardians, officials, and anyone the owner directly asks to retrieve the slave. However, those who are already under the owner's maintenance or whose duty it is to return runaways are not entitled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the eleven categories
List each category: spouses, guardian (wasi) returning to orphan, caretaker of orphan, one explicitly asked by owner (with condition of verbal agreement), sultan, police chief (shahna), guard (khafir), and subcategories making eleven.
The text says 'fawāridu iḥdā 'asharah' — so there are eleven.
2
Understand the condition for the asked person
For the one whom the owner asks to retrieve the slave, he must verbally agree (say 'na'am') to be entitled. This is based on a promise of assistance.
Al-Tatarkhaniyya conditions the verbal agreement.
3
Note the exception
If the returner is already under the owner's maintenance (e.g., a servant) or is obliged by duty to return runaways (e.g., a guard), he does not qualify for the reward.
The exception is stated in 'lā yastahiqqu' for those who safeguard the owner's property or serve him.
4
Recognize the scope
The reward is due from the owner whether the returner is adult or child, free or slave, and whether he returns personally or via a deputy.
These details are expanded in the next part of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإباق
قد
الزوجين إلى الآخر، وكذا يرد عليه لو رده الوصي إلى اليتيم وكذا من يعول اليتيم إذا رد قد ابقه وليس بوصي، وكذا يرد عليه لو كان مالكه قد استعاذ به كما لو قال لرجل إن عبدي أبق فإذا وجدته فخذه كما في فتح القدير وشرط في التتارخانية أن يقول له نعم معللاً بأنه وعد له الإعانة وكذا يرد عليه لو رده السلطان أو الشحنة أو الخفير لوجوب الفعل عليهم فالوارد إحدى عشرة فلو قال إذا كان الراد يحفظ مال السيد أو يخدمه أو استعان به لسلم من الإيراد كما لا يخفى. وشمل ما إذا كان الراد بالغاً أو صبياً حراً أو عبداً لأن الصبي من أهل استحقاق الأجر بالعمل وكذا العبد إلا أن الجعل لمولاه لأنه ليس من أهل ملك المال؛ كذا في البدائع. وشمل ما إذا رده بنفسه أو نائبه. قال في المحيط : أخذ آبقاً من مسيرة سفر فدفعه إلى رجل وأمره أن يأتي به إلى مولاه وأن يأخذ منه الجعل جاز. وذكر في آخر الباب لو أخذ عبداً آبقاً فاغتصبه منه رجل وجاء به لمولاه فدفعه إليه وأخذ جعله ثم جاء الذي أخذه فأقام البينة أنه أخذه من مسيرة ثلاثة أيام فإنه يأخذ من مولاه الجعل ثانياً على الغاصب بما دفع إليه لأنه أخذه بغير حق .اهـ. وأطلق في السيد فشمل البالغ والصبي فيجعل الجعل في ماله وشمل ما إذا كان متعدداً فالجعل على قدر النصيب، فلو كان البعض غائباً فليس للحاضر أن يأخذه حتى يعطي تمام الجعل، ولا يكون متبرعاً. بنصيب الغائب فيرجع عليه. وأطلق في المردود فشمل ما إذا كان صغيراً فهو كالكبير؛ ذكره الحاكم في الكافي لكن ذكر بعده : وإذا أبقت الأمة ولها صبي رضيع فردهما رجل كان له جعل واحد، فإن كان ابنها غلاماً قد قارب الحلم فله الجعل ثمانون درهماً .اهـ. وقيد ولد الآبقة بالمراهق ولم قيد أولاً فالظاهر أن الصغير إن لم يكن تبعاً لأحد أبويه لا يشترط أن يكون مراهقاً وإلا فهو شرط لكن لا بد من تقييده بالعقل . قال في التتارخانية وما ذكر من الجواب في الصغير محمول على ما إذا كان يعقل الإباق، أما إذا كان لا يعقل فهو ضال لا يستحق له الجعل اهـ. وفي المصباح : الجغل بالضم الأجر يقال جعلت له جعلك، والجعالة بكسر الجيم وبعضهم يحكي التثليث والجعيلة مثل الكريمة لغات في الجعل اهـ .
The book of runaway slaves. He said in al-Tatarkhaniyya: what is mentioned of the answer regarding the child is carried upon when he is sane regarding running away, but if he is not sane, he is a lost person, he does not deserve the reward. End. And in al-Misbah: al-jighl with damm (means) wage; it is said: I made a reward for you; and al-ju'alah with kasr of jeem and some relate three vowels, and al-ju'eelah like al-karimah, all dialects for al-ju'l. End.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq opens the chapter on runaway slaves (Kitab al-Ibaq). It enumerates eleven categories of persons whose return of a runaway slave entitles them to a reward (ju'l) from the owner, unless they are under the owner's maintenance or obliged to return by virtue of their position. The list includes: the spouse, the guardian (wasi) returning to the orphan, the caretaker of the orphan, one who was explicitly asked by the owner to retrieve the slave (with the condition that he verbally agrees), the sultan, the police chief (shahna), and the guard (khafir). The passage also clarifies that the returner may be an adult or a minor, free or slave, though if a slave returns a runaway, the reward goes to his master. It also covers the case of a female slave with a suckling child, stating that both are considered one return, but if the child is near puberty, a separate reward of eighty dirhams applies. The commentary then discusses the capacity of a minor returner, emphasizing that he must understand the concept of running away; otherwise, he is considered a lost person and does not qualify for the reward. Finally, it defines the term ju'l as an agreed wage. This lesson establishes the general rules of entitlement to the reward.

Key Terms
الجعل (al-ju'l): The reward or compensation paid by the owner to the person who returns the runaway slave.
الراد (al-radd): The person who returns the runaway slave to its owner.
الآبق (al-abiq): A slave who has run away from his master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The sultan
D) The guardian (wasi) returning the orphan's slave

Key Takeaway
The reward for returning a runaway slave is due to eleven specific categories of returners, excluding those already under the owner's service or duty.
