The Hanafi Dispute on Declaring a Missing Person Dead
Commentary on multiple Hanafi opinions with tarjīḥ

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the multiple Hanafi opinions on the time limit for presuming a missing person dead, explain the original zahir al-riwayah position (based on peers), and evaluate the mufta bihi view that leaves the period to the judge's discretion.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school originally tied death presumption to peers, but practicality led to fixed-year estimates; the chosen view leaves it to judicial discretion.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the rich internal Hanafi debate over how long a missing person must be absent before being declared dead. While the original school position (zahir al-riwayah) required verifying the death of the missing person's peers, later scholars found this impractical and proposed various fixed time limits from 60 to 120 years. The commentator ultimately prefers Shams al-A'immah's view that no fixed period should be set, leaving the matter to the judge's discretion. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school balances textual authority with practical necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the zahir al-riwayah position
The original school ruling is that death is determined by the death of the missing person's peers (aqrān), not a fixed number of years. If even one peer remains alive, the missing person is not declared dead.
Peers are those of similar age; the soundest view limits peers to the same country.
2
List the fixed-year opinions
Later scholars offered multiple estimates: 60 years (mutā'akhkhirūn), 70 (Ibn al-Humām), 80 (reported in al-Tatarkhāniyya), 90 (author of Kanz, fatwa given), 100 (Abū Yūsuf chosen by Abū Bakr ibn Ḥāmid), and 120 (from Ḥasan narration, chosen by al-Qudūrī).
Each estimate reflects a different assessment of the ghalib (prevalent) maximum lifespan.
3
Understand the rationale for each fixed-year view
The differences are based on divergent opinions about the ghalib: some consider the maximum lifespan (e.g., 90, 100, 120), others the absolute prevalent lifespan (60), and Ibn al-Humām relied on the hadith that most of the ummah live between 60 and 70.
The hadith 'A'mār ummatī mā bayna al-sittīn ilā al-sab'īn' is cited in support of 70.
4
Analyze Shams al-A'immah's view
Shams al-A'immah al-Ḥalwānī held that no fixed period should be set; instead, the judge should rule case by case based on maslahah. The commentator declares this view 'al-mukhtār' (the chosen one).
This view is considered most consistent with fiqh methodology because setting limits by mere opinion is not valid.
5
Examine the legal consequences of the death ruling
Once the judge rules the missing person dead (at whatever period), the wife begins her iddah and inherits from that moment, and the missing person's mudabbars and ummahat awlād are freed. He does not inherit from someone who died before his own death was ruled.
The ruling is considered from that moment as if the death was known then (ḥukmī is treated like ḥaqīqī).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وحكم بموته بعد تسعين سنة) لأنه الغاية في زماننا والحياة بعدها نادر فلا عبرة للنادر، وقد وقع الاختلاف في هذه واختلف الترجيح فظاهر الرواية وهو المذهب أنه مقدر بموت الأقران في السن لأن من النوادر أن يعيش الإنسان بعد موت أقرانه فلا ينبغي الحكم عليه، فإذا بقي منهم واحد لا يحكم بموته. واختلفوا في المراد بموت أقرانه فقيل من جميع البلاد، وقيل من بلده وهو الأصح ؛ كذا في الذخيرة واختار المؤلف التقدير بالتسعين بتقديم التاء على السين تبعاً لابن الفضل وهو الأرفق كما في الهداية وفي الذخيرة وعليه الفتوى، وعن أبي يوسف تقديره بمائة سنة واختاره أبو بكر بن حامد وفي رواية الحسن عن الإمام بمائة وعشرين سنة واختاره القدوري واختار المتأخرون ستين سنة، واختار المحقق ابن الهمام سبعين سنة، واختار شمس الأئمة أن لا يقدر بشيء لأنه أليق بطريق الفقه لأن نصب المقادير بالرأي لا تكون وفي الهداية أنه الأقيس وفوضه بعضهم إلى القاضي فأي وقت رأى المصلحة حكم بموته. قال الشارح: وهو المختار والحاصل أن الاختلاف ما جاء إلا اختلاف الرأي أي في أن الغالب هذا في الطول أو مطلقاً، والعجب من المشايخ كيف يختارون خلاف ظاهر المذهب مع أنه واجب الاتباع على مقلدي أبي حنيفة والإمام محمد لم يعتبر السنين وإنما اعتبره المتقدمون ،بعده وقال الصدر الشهيد في شرحه : ما قال محمد أحوط كما في التتارخانية ولقد صدق من قال كثرة المقالات تؤذن بكثرة الجهالات ومن الغريب ما نقله في التتارخانية أنه مقدر بثمانين سنة وعليه الفتوى. قوله : (وتعتد امرأته وورث منه حينئذ لا (قبله أي حين حكم بموته بمضي هذه المدة والظرف قيد للحكمين كأنه من ذلك الوقت معاينة إذ الحكمي معتبر بالحقيقي وكذا يحكم بعتق مدبريه وأمهات أولاده في ذلك الوقت كما في الحاوي قوله: (ولا يرث من أحد مات) أي قبل الحكم بموته لأن بقاءه حياً في ذلك الوقت باستصحاب الحال وهو لا يصلح حجة للاستحقاق، من مات قوله : (والحاصل الخ) هذا الحاصل ذكره في الفتح وبيانه أن اختلافهم في تقديره بتسعين أو بمائة أو بمائة وعشرين مبني على اختلاف الرأي في الغالب في طول العمر، فبعضهم رأى أن الغالب في طول العمر أي الغالب في نهاية ما يعيش إليه الإنسان تسعون فقدوه بها، وبعضهم رأى أن الغالب فيه المائة فقدر بها وهكذا وبعضهم نظر إلى الغالب مطلقاً أي لا من حيث كونه أطول ما يعيش إليه الإنسان بل من حيث كونه الغالب في أصل الطول وهو الستون فإن من يعيش إلى الستين أكثر ممن يعيش إلى التسعين أو أكثر. قال في الفتح: وعندي الأحسن سبعين لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «أعمار أمتي ما بين الستين إلى «السبعين» فكانت المنتهى غالباً .اهـ. قوله : (والعجب من المشايخ قال في النهر : أنت خبير بأن التفحص عن موت الأقران غير ممكن أو فيه حرج فعن هذا اختار المشايخ تقديره بالسن اهـ . قلت : وقد يكون هذا التقدير تفسيراً لظاهر الرواية بأن المراد منه
His statement: (And he rules his death after ninety years) because it is the maximum in our time and life after it is rare, so no attention is paid to the rare. And there has been disagreement on this and the preferred opinion differs. The zahir al-riwayah and the madhhab is that it is estimated by the death of peers in age, because it is rare for a person to live after the death of his peers, so one should not rule on him. If even one of them remains, he is not ruled dead. And they differed on the meaning of the death of his peers: it was said from all countries, and it was said from his own country, which is the soundest view. This is in al-Dhakhira. And the author chose the estimation of ninety, with the ta' before the sin, following Ibn al-Fadl, and it is more convenient as in al-Hidaya and al-Dhakhira, and the fatwa is upon it. And from Abu Yusuf: his estimation is one hundred years, chosen by Abu Bakr ibn Hamid. And in the narration of Hasan from the Imam: one hundred and twenty years, chosen by al-Quduri. And the later scholars chose sixty years. And the investigator Ibn al-Humam chose seventy years. And Shams al-A'immah chose that it should not be estimated at all, because it is more appropriate to the way of fiqh, because setting limits by opinion is not valid. And in al-Hidaya, it is the more analogical, and some delegated it to the judge, so whenever he sees maslahah, he rules his death. The commentator said: And it is the chosen view. The summary is that the difference is only difference of opinion, i.e., regarding whether this is the prevalent in length or absolutely. And amazing is how the scholars choose contrary to the zahir al-madhhab while it is obligatory to follow for the muqallids of Abu Hanifa, and Imam Muhammad did not consider years, but rather the later scholars considered them. And al-Sadr al-Shahid said in his commentary: What Muhammad said is more cautious, as in al-Tatarkhaniyya. And truth is said: many opinions indicate many ignorances. And among the strange things is what was transmitted in al-Tatarkhaniyya: that it is estimated by eighty years, and fatwa is upon it. His statement: (And his wife observes iddah and inherits from him at that time, not before) i.e., at the time he is ruled dead after the passage of this period, and the adverb is a qualifier for both rulings, as if it is from that time seen, for the legal is considered by the real. And likewise, one rules the emancipation of his mudabbars and ummahat awlad at that time, as in al-Hawi. His statement: (And he does not inherit from anyone who dies) i.e., before the rule of his death, because his being alive at that time is by istishab al-hal, which is not a valid proof for entitlement. His statement: (And the summary, etc.) This summary is mentioned in al-Fath, and its explanation is that their difference in estimating by ninety, or one hundred, or one hundred and twenty is based on difference of opinion regarding the prevalent in the length of life. So some saw that the prevalent in the length of life, i.e., the prevalent in the end of what a person lives to, is ninety, so they estimated by it. And some saw that the prevalent is one hundred, so they estimated by it. And some looked at the prevalent absolutely, i.e., not in terms of it being the longest a person lives to, but in terms of it being the prevalent in the basic length, which is sixty, for those who live to sixty are more than those who live to ninety or more. He said in al-Fath: And in my view, the best is seventy, because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'The ages of my ummah are between sixty and seventy', so the end is prevalent. End quote. His statement: (And the amazement at the scholars) He said in al-Nahr: You are aware that investigating the death of peers is not possible or involves hardship, so for this reason the scholars chose estimation by years. End quote. I say: This estimation may be an interpretation of the zahir al-riwayah, that the meaning is ...
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It discusses the period after which a missing person may be declared dead. The commentator first explains the matn that the judge rules death after ninety years. However, he immediately notes that the zahir al-riwayah (the primary transmission) of the school is that it is based on the death of the missing person's peers, not a fixed number of years. 'Peers' here means those of similar age; if even one peer remains alive, the missing person is not declared dead. There is a subsidiary dispute on whether peers are worldwide or just from the same country; the soundest view is the latter. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq (likely al-Nasafi) chose ninety years following Ibn al-Fadl, and according to some sources the fatwa is on that. Then the commentator lists numerous other opinions: Abu Yusuf: 100 years; a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa: 120 years; the later scholars (mutakhkhirin): 60 years; Ibn al-Humam: 70 years; Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani: no fixed number, left to the judge's discretion. The commentator states that Shams al-A'immah's view is the chosen one (al-mukhtar). He explains that all these differences are based on different assessments of the ghalib (prevalent) lifespan: some consider the maximum prevalent (90 or 100), others consider the absolute prevalent (60). A hadith is cited: 'The ages of my ummah are between sixty and seventy,' supporting the view of 70 years. The commentator expresses amazement that later scholars chose fixed numbers contrary to the zahir al-madhhab, which required verification of peers' deaths. However, he acknowledges, citing al-Nahr, that investigating peers' deaths is practically impossible or extremely difficult, which led later scholars to adopt fixed years. The passage then describes the consequences of the death ruling: the wife begins her iddah and inherits from that moment, and the missing person's mudabbars and ummahat awlad are freed. He does not inherit from anyone who died before his own death was ruled.

Key Terms
أقران (aqrān): Peers of the missing person, i.e., people of similar age and circumstances.
ظاهر الرواية (zāhir al-riwāyah): The primary and most authoritative transmission of the Hanafi school, typically from Muhammad al-Shaybani's six books.
غالب (ghālib): The prevalent, common, or most frequent occurrence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator in this passage, which view is considered the chosen (mukhtār) one for declaring a missing person dead?
A) 90 years
B) 100 years
C) No fixed period, left to the judge's discretion
D) 70 years

Key Takeaway
The original Hanafi rule based on peers' deaths was modified by later scholars for practicality, but the preferred view returns to flexibility by leaving the period to the judge's discretion.

Using Joint Property Without Permission: Hanafi Rulings
Listing of furu' (branches) on joint property use

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for using a shared animal, house, land, and measured goods when a partner is absent, and identify the underlying principle of preventing disuse without causing harm.

Core Idea
Use of joint property without permission is allowed only when it does not harm the partner or the property.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a series of practical rulings for a common scenario: one co-owner is absent, and the other needs to use the jointly owned property. The rulings differ by property type—animals, houses, land, and goods—reflecting a balance between the absent partner's rights and the need to avoid letting the property lie idle. Understanding these distinctions is essential for applying Hanafi fiqh in everyday partnerships.

Guided Path
1
Identify the property categories
List the four types of joint property mentioned: riding animal, house/servant, land, and measured goods (by weight or volume).
Each category has a different ruling based on the nature of use.
2
Recall the default rule
The default rule is that using another's property without permission is not allowed. The Hanafi rulings here are exceptions based on necessity and custom.
The absent partner's consent is assumed if it would be in their interest.
3
Distinguish harmful vs. beneficial uses
Riding an animal causes wear (harm), so it is prohibited. Living in a house or using a servant without causing damage is beneficial and allowed. Cultivating land is allowed only if it improves the land.
The key criterion is whether the use benefits or harms the joint property.
4
Apply the rule to measured goods
For goods sold by weight or volume, the present partner may separate his share and use it, as this does not harm the remainder. If the remainder perishes unexpectedly, it is a shared loss.
This shows the principle of 'ghunm bi al-ghurm' (profit with liability) implicitly.
5
Note the fatwa hierarchy
The text explicitly mentions 'al-muftā bihi' for land cultivation, indicating this is the relied-upon position. Other rulings are also from the madhhab's authoritative sources like al-Khaniyya.
Be aware that later fatwa rulings may differ from the text of the early manuals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الثاني ففيه تفصيل؛ ففي الدابة المشتركة لا يركبها بغير إذن شريكه، وفي البيت له أن يسكن كله في غيبة شريكه وكذا الخادم، ولا يلزمه أجرة حصة شريكه، ولو كانت الدار معدة للاستغلال وفي الأرض له أن يزرعها كلها على المفتى به إن كان الزرع ينفعها، فإذا جاء شريكه زرعها مثل تلك المدة، وإن كان الزرع ينقصها أو الترك ينفعها فليس له أن يزرعها وفي الكيلي والوزني له أن يعزل حصته بغيبة شريكه وينتفع بها ولا شيء عليه إن سلم الباقي فإن هلك قبل التسليم إلى شريكه هلك عليهما، وتمامه في جامع الفصولين من الفصل الثالث والثلاثين من الانتفاع بالمشترك. وفي الخانية : ولو كان بينهما شركة في مال خلطاه ليس لواحد منهما أن يسافر بالمال بغير إذن الشريك، فإن سافر به فهلك، فإن كان له حمل ومؤنة ضمن وإن لم يكن له حمل ومؤنة لا يضمن اهـ.
As for the second, it has details. In a jointly owned animal, he may not ride it without his partner's permission. In a house, he may live in all of it in the absence of his partner, and likewise a servant. And he is not liable for the rent of his partner's share. If the house is prepared for exploitation, and in land, he may cultivate all of it according to the fatwa if cultivation benefits it; when his partner comes, he (the partner) cultivates it for a similar period. If cultivation diminishes it or leaving it benefits it, he may not cultivate it. In items measured by weight or volume, he may separate his share in his partner's absence and benefit from it, and nothing is due from him if he delivers the remainder; if it perishes before delivery to his partner, it is destroyed on both. Its completion is in Jami' al-Fusulayn from the thirty-third chapter on benefiting from joint property. In al-Khaniyya: If they have a partnership in mixed property, neither may travel with the money without the partner's permission; if he travels with it and it perishes, if he had profit or expense then he is liable, otherwise he is not liable. End.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It presents a series of rulings (furu') regarding the use of jointly owned property when one partner is absent. The rulings are based on istihsan (juristic preference) and consider the practical need to prevent disuse of property. The present partner may use the house, servant, and land without paying rent, but riding the animal is prohibited because it causes more wear. The fatwa position on land cultivation is conditional on cultivation being beneficial. If the shared asset is measured, the present partner may isolate his share. The additional quote from al-Khaniyya addresses traveling with joint money.

Key Terms
المشاع (al-mushā'): Jointly owned property that is undivided (shāyi').
المفتى به (al-muftā bihi): The relied-upon position for giving fatwa, indicating the preferred ruling in the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must pay rent for the absent partner's share.
B) He may live in the entire house without paying rent.
C) He may only live in his share as determined by measurement.
D) He must seek permission from the absent partner first.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of using joint property without permission hinges on whether the use benefits the property and does not harm the absent partner's interest; otherwise, permission is required.

Using Joint Property: Rulings and Intra-Hanafi Disputes
Extended rulings with intra-Hanafi differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for a present partner's use of shared property (house, servant, animal, land) and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on cultivation and dwelling.

Core Idea
In a shared house, the present partner is considered to dwell in his own property—no rent is due.

When two partners own an undivided house and one is absent, the present partner may need to use the entire property. The Hanafi school provides detailed rules: dwelling is freely allowed, but riding an animal is not. An intra-Hanafi difference arises regarding land cultivation and the house when it risks ruin. The underlying principle is that for dwelling, the shared asset is treated as each partner's complete property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three shared items and their rulings
From the passage, list the three items: house, servant, animal. For each, state the basic ruling from the agreed Hanafi position: present partner may dwell in entire house, may use servant for his share, may not ride the animal.
The ruling for the animal is based on harm (darar) due to varied riding styles.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on house and land
Imam Muhammad allows the present partner to live in the entire house if he fears ruin. Abu Hanifa restricts land cultivation to the present partner's share only, but allows full dwelling in the house.
The text uses 'H' for Abu Hanifa and names Muhammad directly.
3
Extract the underlying principle (asl)
The passage states that for dwelling and its accessories, the shared house is considered as if each partner owns it completely. This prevents the utility from being lost and is the basis for no rent being due.
This principle is based on necessity (darura) and istihsan.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, if a partner is absent for a long time, the present partner can live in the entire house without paying rent. However, he cannot cultivate the absent partner's land without permission (Abu Hanifa's view) unless the land would be ruined (Muhammad's view).
The earlier passage mentioned 'on the fatwa' for land cultivation if beneficial, suggesting Muhammad's view may be preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دار بينهما غير مقسومة غاب أحدهما وسع الحاضر أن يسكن بقدر حصته فيسكن الدار كلها وكذا خادم بينهما غاب أحدهما فللحاضر أن يستخدمه بحصته، وفي الدابة لا يركبها الحاضر لتفاوت الناس في الركوب لا السكنى والاستخدام فيتضرر الغائب بركوبها لا بهمان عن محمد رحمه الله : للحاضر أن يسكن كل الدار لو خاف خرابها لو لم يسكنها. وعن ح رحمه الله : ليس للحاضر في الأرض أن يزرع بقدر نصيبه وفي الدار له أن يسكنها (بر) أن له ذلك في الوجهين فلو سكن الدار أحد شريكيهما بغيبة الآخر لا يلزمه الأجر ولو أعدت للاستغلال، والأصل أن الدار المشتركة في حق السكنى وتوابعه تجعل كملك لكل من الشريكين على الكمال إذ لو لم تجعل كذلك. يمتنع كل منهما من دخول وقعود ووضع أمتعة فيتعطل عليهما منافع ملكهما وهو لم يجز فصار الحاضر ساكناً في ملك نفسه فكيف يلزم الأجر؟ اهـ . وهذه المسائل كثيرة الوقوع فلتحفظ.
An undivided house between them; one of them is absent: the present one may live in proportion to his share, so he lives in the entire house. Similarly, a servant between them, one absent: the present may use him for his share. As for the animal, the present may not ride it because people differ in riding, unlike dwelling and using, so the absent would be harmed by riding it. From Muhammad: The present may live in the entire house if he fears its ruin if he does not live in it. From Abu Hanifa: The present may not cultivate the land beyond his share, but in the house he may live in it. That he may do so in both aspects. So if one of the two partners lives in the house in the absence of the other, he is not liable for rent even if it was prepared for exploitation. The principle is that the shared house in terms of dwelling and its accessories is considered as the complete property of each partner, because if it were not so, each would be prevented from entering, sitting, and placing belongings, and the benefits of their property would be interrupted – which is not permissible. So the present dwells in his own property; how then would rent be due? End. These issues are frequently occurring, so be mindful.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on joint property. It presents the rulings on a shared house, servant, and animal when one partner is absent. The present partner may live in the entire house and use the servant fully, but cannot ride the animal. Imam Muhammad adds a condition: if the house would fall into ruin from disuse, the present partner may live in the entire house. Abu Hanifa (indicated by 'H') restricts land cultivation to the share of the present partner only. The passage then states the fundamental principle (asl) that for purposes of dwelling, the shared house is considered as if each partner owns it completely. This is based on necessity (darura) and istihsan – otherwise, none could use the property effectively. The ruling that no rent is due is derived from this principle.

Key Terms
ح (ḥā'): Abbreviation for Abu Hanifa (رحمه الله).
الأصل (al-aṣl): The fundamental principle or legal basis from which rulings are derived.
الدار المشتركة (al-dār al-mushtaraka): An undivided house owned jointly by two or more partners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

The Pillar of Contractual Partnership: Offer and Acceptance
Defining shirkat al-'aqd and its pillar of offer and acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of shirkat al-'aqd, identify its pillar (rukn) of offer and acceptance, and explain why any wording indicating mutual consent suffices.

Core Idea
A contractual partnership is formed by offer and acceptance — the specific word 'sharaktuka' is not required; any clear indication of mutual consent suffices.

In this passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq, we examine the second type of partnership: shirkat al-'aqd (contractual partnership). The author explains that its essential pillar is offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul) that indicate mutual agreement to share profits. Importantly, the Hanafi school does not require a specific formula; any expression that clearly conveys the intention to form a partnership is sufficient. This flexibility makes business transactions easier in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal status
Recognise that shirkat al-'aqd is a partnership formed by mutual agreement, distinct from co-ownership. Its ruling is ja'iz (permissible) as a contract.
2
Locate the pillar (rukn)
The text states that the rukn is offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul). These two elements constitute the pillar; without them the contract does not exist.
Offer and acceptance must indicate mutual consent to share profits.
3
Understand the flexibility in wording
The author emphasises that the contract is concluded by whatever indicates partnership, not specifically the phrase 'sharaktuka'. Any words or even actions that clearly show agreement suffice.
Example given: handing over money with instructions to invest and share profit is sufficient.
4
Examine the scope of the partnership
The phrase 'in such-and-such' (fi kadha) can be specific (e.g. a particular trade) or general (all trades). The text criticises the view that general scope is restricted to mufawadah and specific to 'inan, because 'inan partnerships can also be general.
This shows the Hanafi position that the classification depends on the terms, not the label.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider two entrepreneurs: A says 'I will invest 1000, you invest the same, and we share profits equally.' B accepts. The partnership is valid even if the word 'sharaktuka' is not used.
The contract is concluded by the mutual exchange of offers and acceptance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشركة العقد أن يقول أحدهما شاركتك في كذا ويقبل الآخر وهي مفاوضة إن ... قوله: (وشركة العقد أن يقول أحدهما شاركتك في كذا ويقبل الآخر) بيان للنوع الثاني ومقصوده بيان ركنها من الإيجاب والقبول الدالين عليها لا خصوص شاركتك لأنها عقد من العقود فينعقد بما يدل عليه، ولهذا لو دفع ألفاً إلى رجل وقال أخرج مثلها واشتر وما كان من ربح فهو بيننا وقبل الآخر وأخذها وفعل انعقدت الشركة. وقوله «في كذا» أي في شيء لأن كذا كناية عن الشيء؛ كذا في القاموس وذلك الشيء أعم من أن يكون خاصاً كالبز والبقل أو عاماً كما إذا شاركه في عموم التجارات، وتخصيص العموم بالمفاوضة والخصوص بالعنان كما في فتح القدير لا وجه له لأن العنان قد تكون عامة أيضاً ولذا قال في البزازية : شركة العنان عامة بأن يشتركا في أنواع التجارات كلها وخاصة وهو أن يشتركا في شيء الخانية قبيل كتاب الإقرار ثم في الدار المشتركة إذا كان أحدهما غائباً فإن للحاضر أن يسكن كل الدار بقدر حصته. وفي رواية له أن يسكن من الدار قدر حصته ولو خاف أن تخرب الدار بترك السكني كان له أن يسكن كل الدار اهـ. قوله: (فأشرك في طحنها مصدر بمعنى اسم المفعول أي مطحونها. قوله : (جاز وله الخيار مقتضاه أن يجوز على أنه بيع ويشكل ذلك بأن البيع بلا . معرفة
And contractual partnership (shirkat al-'aqd) is that one of them says 'I partner with you in such-and-such' and the other accepts, and it is a partnership of mufawadah if ... The author's statement: '(And contractual partnership is that one of them says I partner with you in such-and-such and the other accepts)' is an explanation of the second type, and its purpose is to explain its pillar (rukn) consisting of offer and acceptance indicating it, not specifically the word 'sharaktuka' because it is a contract among contracts, so it is concluded by whatever indicates it. Hence, if someone gave a thousand to a man and said 'Bring out the like and buy, and whatever profit is between us' and the other accepted, took it, and did so, the partnership is concluded. His statement 'in such-and-such' means 'in a thing' because 'kadha' is a word for 'thing'; also in the Qamus. That thing is general, whether specific like cloth or greens, or general as when he partners with him in all trades. The specification of the general as mufawadah and the specific as 'inan, as in Fath al-Qadir, has no basis because 'inan may also be general. Hence al-Bazzaziyya said: Partnership 'inan is general by their sharing in all types of trades, and specific by sharing in a thing. Al-Khaniyya, before the chapter on iqrar, then: In a shared house if one is absent, the present may live in the entire house according to his share. In one narration, he may live in the house according to his share, and if he fears the house will be ruined by leaving it empty, he may live in the entire house. End. His statement: 'So he included him in its grinding' (fa'ashraka fi tahniha) is a masdar in the sense of ism maf'ul, meaning its ground flour. His statement: 'It is valid and he has the option' (jaza wa lahu al-khiyar) implies that it is valid as a sale, but this is problematic because a sale without ... knowledge.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage defines the second type of partnership, shirkat al-'aqd (contractual partnership). Its pillar (rukn) is offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul) that indicate mutual consent to share profits. The specific wording 'sharaktuka' is not required; any words indicating partnership suffice. The author gives an example: a person gives money to another to invest in a specific way. The text also clarifies the scope of 'in such-and-such,' which can be specific or general. It criticizes a view that restricts mufawadah to general and 'inan to specific, arguing that 'inan can also be general. The commentary then returns to a previous example about grinding grain, where including a partner in the grinding process gives that partner a share of the final product. The passage ends abruptly discussing the option (khiyar) in such transactions.

Key Terms
شركة العقد (shirkat al-'aqd): Contractual partnership formed by mutual agreement to share profits, as opposed to shirkat al-milk (co-ownership).
الإيجاب والقبول (al-ījāb wa al-qabūl): Offer and acceptance, the two components of the contractual pillar (rukn).
مفاوضة (mufāwaḍah): A type of partnership where partners are equal in capital, profit, and authority, and are agents and guarantors for each other.
عنان (‘inān): A partnership where partners may have unequal capital and profit shares; they are not guarantors for each other beyond the partnership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the pillar (rukn) of contractual partnership (shirkat al-'aqd)?
A) Equal capital contribution.
B) Written contract.
C) Offer and acceptance indicating mutual consent.
D) Profit-sharing ratio of 50:50.

Key Takeaway
The essence of a contractual partnership is mutual consent expressed through offer and acceptance; no specific wording is required.

Craftsmen Partnership: Validity and Conditions
Commentary on partnership validity and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid craftsmen partnership and explain why unity of work is not required.

Core Idea
A tailor and a dyer can partner because the partnership is based on mutual guarantee, not identical trades.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that the partnership of craftsmen (shirkat al-sana'i') is valid regardless of whether the trades are identical or different. The ruling is based on istihsan, which overrides strict qiyas. We will identify the conditions (halal work, legally claimable) and the proof structure that permits unequal profit shares.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a partnership between two craftsmen (e.g., tailors or dye) who agree to jointly accept work and share earnings. The ruling is that it is valid (ja'iz).
2
Locate the dalil for permissibility
The commentary states the reason: the goal is acquisition (tahsil), which is possible through mutual agency. Each partner is an agent (wakil) in half and principal (asil) in half, so the acquired wealth becomes shared.
This is based on istihsan, as qiyas would require stricter conditions.
3
Identify the conditions
The work must be halal and legally claimable (mustahaqq). Unity of work or place is not required. The partnership can be valid even if one partner is not proficient.
Examples: teachers, tailors with different tools, but not work that cannot be enforced like brokerage or humming recitals.
4
Analyze profit sharing
Profit sharing can be equal or unequal. The correct view is that unequal shares are permitted because profit is based on the guarantee of work (daman al-aml), not the actual work done.
From Fath al-Qadir.
5
Note the ikhtilaf on conditions
Some conditions (like stipulating a specific fixed amount for one partner) may invalidate the partnership, but most conditions do not. The partnership is not invalidated by stipulating preference in loss.
The text says the apparent view is that it is not nullified by most conditions.

التنصيص على المفاوضة لم يوجد ونفاذ الإقرار موجب من أحدهما يبيع الشركة أن يجلس آخر على دكانه فيطرح عليه العمل بالنصف والقياس أن لا تجوز لأن . العمل ومن الآخر الحانوت واستحسن جوازها لأن التقبل من صاحب (والمعازي بالزمزمة) قال في القاموس : العزا الصبر أو حسنه كالتعزوة، والزمزمة الصوت البعيد له صوت الرعد، والمراد القراءة في المأتم الذي يصنع للأموات مع التمطيط قال ابن الشحنة في شرح دوي وتتابع
A trust and acceptance: if two tailors or a tailor and a dyer partner on the condition that they both accept work and the earnings are between them... And he died without clarifying with whom he deposited, there is no liability on him. The third: the judge if he took the orphan's wealth and deposited it with someone else and died without clarifying with whom he deposited, there is no liability on him. As for one of the two partners in a full partnership (mufawada), if the wealth was with him and he did not clarify the state of the wealth that was with him; some jurists mentioned that he is not liable and referred it to the original partnership, and that is a mistake. Rather, the correct view is that he is liable for his partner's share; thus in Fatawa Qadikhan from the book of Waqf. And by this it becomes clear that what is in Fath al-Qadir and some fatwas is weak, and that the partner is liable upon death due to ignorance, whether the partnership is 'inan or mufawada. His statement: (and acceptance, if two tailors or a tailor and a dyer partner on the condition that they accept work and the earnings are between them) with a damma (raising) as an 'atf on 'mufawada', is an explanation of the partnership of craftsmen. Its apparent meaning is that acceptance and work are other than mufawada and 'inan, but we have previously mentioned the contrary. In al-Bazzaziyya: the partnership of acceptance and work may be mufawada or 'inan; 'inan is what is in a specific trade, and mufawada is what is in all trades. End. And the benefit of it being mufawada will come later. This type of partnership is permitted because the goal is acquisition, and that is possible through agency, because he is an agent in half and a principal in half, so partnership is realized in the acquired wealth. And his statement 'or a tailor and a dyer' indicates that unity of work is not required. They said: unity of place is also not required, because the reason that permits it, which we mentioned, does not vary. So the meaning of his statement 'if two tailors partner' is two craftsmen, even if by legal construction (hukman), whether their work is the same or different, provided it is permissible work that can be legally claimed. This includes if two teachers partner for teaching children and instructing in writing and Quran, for the chosen view is its permissibility as in al-Bazzaziyya; and if one has a laundry tool and the other has a house, they partner to work in this house on condition that earnings are between them, it is permissible. Similarly for all crafts. And if one has the laundry tool and the other does the work, it is invalid, the profit is for the worker, and he owes the owner of the tool its rental equivalent; thus in al-Bazzaziyya. In al-Qunyah: three porters partnered on condition that one fills the sack, the second closes its mouth, and the third loads it and carries it to the client's house, with the wage divided equally among them; this partnership is invalid. Radi Allahu anhu said: its invalidity is due to these conditions, for the partnership of porters is valid if they partner in accepting work and doing it all together. And if they partner in accepting the books of pilgrims on condition that whatever Allah provides them with, it is half and half, this partnership is valid. End. And we said: even if it is by legal construction (hukman) to include the case where they partner in a craft and one of them is not proficient, it is valid, as will come. And we restricted it to permissible work because of what al-Bayri said in his marginalia on al-Ashbah regarding deposit. His statement: (Radi Allahu anhu said: its invalidity is due to these conditions). Al-Ramli said: It was previously stated that it does not become invalid due to invalid conditions. In al-Bazzaziyya: the partnership is nullified by some invalid conditions; so if they stipulate preference in loss, the partnership is not nullified, and it is nullified by stipulating a specific amount for one of them, and the apparent view is that it is not nullified by most conditions. End. And with this the answer can be obtained, contemplate. His statement: (And we said: even if it is by legal construction to include etc.) Al-Nahr said: There is no need for it, since what is shared is the work, not specifically tailoring. That is why they said: some forms of this... between them, and whatever work one of them accepts binds both, and the earnings of one of them is between them, and its existence if they partner without capital. In al-Bazzaziyya: if they partner in forbidden work, it is not valid. End. And we restricted it to being legally claimable because of what is in al-Qunyah: partnership of brokers in their work is not permissible, nor partnership of reciters in recitation with humming in the gathering because it is not claimable against them, nor partnership of beggars because agency in begging is not valid. And because of what is in al-Zahiriyya: if three reciters partner in a gathering and funeral gatherings with humming and melodies, this partnership is invalid because what they partnered for is not claimable against them or any one of them. End. And his statement 'on condition that they accept work' is not a restriction, because if they partner on condition that one of them accepts the goods and the other works, or one accepts the goods and cuts it then gives it to the other for sewing in halves, it is permissible, thus in al-Qunyah. But if the condition is that he only works and he accepts the job, it is permissible; if the condition is that the craftsman does not accept and only does the work, it is not permissible, because when silent, proving it by implication is established, and that is not possible with negation; thus in al-Muhit. And his statement 'and earnings are between them' includes if they stipulate equality or if they stipulate more profit for one of them; it is explicitly stated in al-Bazzaziyya, with the reasoning that work is variable and one may be more skillful. If they stipulate more for the less skilled, there is disagreement. End. And the correct view is permissibility because profit is based on the guarantee of work, not its reality; thus in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Qamus: 'qabila' is accepted (as in nasara, sami'a, daraba), 'qabala' (verbal noun), and 'taqabbala' (n. rare), the noun is 'qibala' and 'taqabbala' (n. rare). End. 'Atlaqaha'? His statement: (And whatever one of them accepts binds both) means each of them is sued for the work and sued for the wage, and the payer is discharged by paying to him. He made it absolute, so it includes if it is mufawada, which is apparent, and if they explicitly state 'inan, and that is istihsan, and qiyas is otherwise because suretyship necessitates mufawada. The reason for istihsan is that this partnership necessitates guarantee; do you not see that whatever work each of them accepts is guaranteed on the other, and thus he deserves the wage due to the efficacy of his acceptance on him, so it runs like mufawada in the guarantee of work and claim of compensation; thus in al-Hidaya. And he only restricted its running like mufawada to these two reasons because otherwise this contract does not run like mufawada, so they said: if one of them acknowledges a debt for the price of soap or potash consumed, or hires a laborer, or pays rent for a house for a past period, he is not believed against his partner except with evidence, and it is binding on him alone, because explicit stipulation of mufawada is not present, and the efficacy of acknowledgement is binding… one of them sells, the partnership is that another sits in his shop and throws work on him in halves, and qiyas is that it is not permissible because… work and the other the shop, and istihsan permits it because acceptance from the shop owner is a work. His statement: (partnership of brokers is not permissible) because the work of brokerage cannot be legally claimed through a contract of hire; even if one hires a broker… for him or buys, the hire is invalid if he did not specify a time, as stated in Ijarah al-Mujtaba. His statement: (and funeral gatherings with humming) said in al-Qamus: 'aza' is patience or its beauty like ta'ziyah; 'zamzama' is a distant sound like thunder; what is meant is recitation in the funeral gathering made for the dead with prolonging.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the partnership of craftsmen (شركة الصنائع) from Kanz al-Daqaiq. It begins by discussing a trust (amana) and acceptance (taqabbul) scenario: if two tailors or a tailor and a dyer partner on condition they both accept work and share earnings, the commentary explains the legal implications. First, it addresses liability when a partner dies without specifying the location of a deposit. Three cases are given: (1) a person who dies without clarifying the deposit – no liability? The text seems corrupt but suggests no liability; (2) a judge who takes an orphan's wealth and deposits it with another, then dies without clarifying – no liability; (3) a partner in a full partnership (مفاوضة) who had the wealth and died without clarifying – the correct view is he is liable for his partner's share, contrary to some jurists. This is supported by Fatawa Qadikhan, and it indicates that the partner's guarantee applies upon death due to ignorance, whether the partnership is 'inan or mufawada.

Then the commentary focuses on the matn phrase 'وتقبل إن اشترك خياطان...'. It explains that the phrase 'بينهما' is in the accusative (رفع) as an 'atf on 'مفاوضة'? Actually the commentary discusses the grammatical analysis. It states that partnership of acceptance and work (شركة التقبل والوجوه) can be either mufawada or 'inan, contrary to the apparent meaning of the matn. The benefit of it being mufawada will come later. This type of partnership is valid because the goal is acquisition, which is possible through mutual agency: each partner is an agent (وكيل) in half and a principal (أصيل) in half, so the acquired wealth becomes shared property.

The author then explains that unity of work (اتحاد العمل) is not required; thus a tailor and a dyer can partner. Similarly, unity of place is not required. What matters is that both are craftsmen (صانعان) even by legal construction (حكماً), i.e., if one is not actually a craftsman but is treated as such. The work must be halal and legally claimable (مستحق). Examples include teachers for children, or one providing a tool and the other a workshop. If one provides only a tool and the other does the work, the partnership is invalid (فاسد), and the worker gets the profit but must pay hire for the tool.

The commentary then gives an example from al-Qunyah: three porters decide that one fills the sack, the second closes it, and the third carries it – this partnership is invalid due to the specific conditions. However, if all porters together accept and do the work, it is valid. Another valid example is partners accepting pilgrims' books and sharing whatever Allah provides equally.

The author adds conditions: the work must be permissible; partnership in forbidden work is invalid. Also, the work must be legally claimable (مستحق), so partnership of brokers (دلالين) is invalid because brokerage cannot be enforced via hire contract if no time limit is set. Similarly, partnership of reciters who recite with humming (زمزمة) in funeral gatherings is invalid because such recitation is not legally claimable against them or anyone.

The condition 'on condition that they accept the work' is not restrictive; variations like one accepting and the other doing the work, or one cutting and the other sewing, are valid if the condition is not prohibitive. However, if the condition specifically prevents the craftsman from accepting work and only does work, it is invalid because the implied agency (اقتضاء) cannot be negated.

Regarding profit sharing, it can be equal or unequal; the correct view is that unequal profit is permitted (الصحيح الجواز) because profit is tied to the guarantee of work (ضمان العمل), not the actual work done. This is from Fath al-Qadir.

The commentary then addresses the scope of 'وكل ما يتقبله أحدهما يلزمهما': each is sued for work and wage, and the client is discharged by paying to either partner. This applies whether the partnership is explicitly mufawada or 'inan, based on istihsan, because the partnership inherently includes guarantee (ضمان). For example, if one partner acknowledges a debt for consumed goods or hires without evidence, it is not binding on the other unless proven, because explicit mufawada was not stipulated.

Finally, it discusses issues like one selling and the other’s shop, and the permissibility via istihsan. Also, it reiterates that partnership of brokers and humming reciters is invalid.

Key Terms
شركة الصنائع (shirkat al-sana'i'): A partnership where two or more craftsmen (e.g., tailors, dyers) jointly accept work and share earnings, with each acting as agent for the other.
التقبل (al-taqabbul): The acceptance of work or contracts; in partnership, it denotes the act of taking on jobs on behalf of the partnership.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that overrides strict qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling.
ضمان العمل (daman al-aml): The guarantee of the work; a partner is responsible for the work accepted by the other, which justifies profit sharing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a valid form of craftsmen partnership?
A) A tailor and a dyer partnering only if they work in the same shop.
B) A tailor and a dyer partnering even if they have different trades.
C) Three porters dividing tasks (fill, tie, carry) and sharing wages equally.
D) A tailor partnering with a broker for finding customers.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates craftsmen partnerships based on istihsan, allowing different trades and unequal profit shares, as long as the work is halal and legally claimable.

Liability and Guarantee in Partnership: Binding Effect of Acceptance
Commentary on binding acceptance and liability upon death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that each partner's acceptance of work binds the other and explain the liability upon death due to ignorance.

Core Idea
In Hanafi partnership, any work accepted by one partner becomes guaranteed on the other, like mufawada.

This section of Bahr al-Raiq addresses the binding effect of acceptance in non-mufawada partnerships. The key ruling is that whatever work one partner accepts binds both, based on istihsan. Additionally, it discusses the liability of a partner who dies without specifying deposited wealth. We will explore the reasoning and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling on acceptance
The text states: 'Whatever work one of them accepts binds both' (wa kull ma yataqabbalahu ahaduhuma yalzamuhuma). This means each partner can be sued for the work and is entitled to the wage, and the client is discharged by paying either.
This applies whether the partnership is mufawada or 'inan, based on istihsan.
2
Understand the istihsan reasoning
Strict qiyas would restrict this binding only to mufawada because suretyship (kafala) requires explicit agreement. But istihsan says the partnership necessarily implies guarantee (daman) because each partner's acceptance is guaranteed on the other, making the partnership run like mufawada in these two aspects: guarantee of work and claim for compensation.
The text quotes al-Hidaya for this reasoning.
3
Identify cases where the binding does not apply
The binding effect is limited to these two aspects. For example, if one partner acknowledges a debt for consumed soap or hires a worker without evidence, it is not binding on the other partner unless proven with evidence, because explicit mufawada is lacking.
This shows that the partnership is not fully mufawada.
4
Analyze the liability upon death
The passage earlier mentions a case where a partner dies without clarifying deposited wealth. Some jurists said he is not liable, but the author (citing Fatawa Qadikhan) declares that as a mistake. The correct view is that he is liable for his partner's share, whether the partnership is 'inan or mufawada.
This is based on the principle that ignorance (tajhil) upon death triggers guarantee.

القاموس : وقد قبل به كنصر وسمع وضرب قبالة وقبلت العامل العمل تقبلاً نادر، والاسم القبالة وتقبله العامل تقبيلاً نادر أيضاً اهـ. أطلقاها قوله : (وكل ما يتقبله أحدهما يلزمهما يعني فيطالب كل واحد منهما بالعمل ويطالب بالأجر ويبرأ الدافع بالدفع إليه أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كانت مفاوضة وهو ظاهر وما إذا وصرحا بالعنان وهو استحسان والقياس خلافه لأن الكفالة تقتضي المفاوضة. وجه الاستحسان أن هذه الشركة مقتضية للضمان ألا ترى أن ما يتقبله كل واحد منهما من العمل مضمون على الآخر ولذا يستحق الأجر بسبب نفاذ تقبله عليه فجرى مجرى المفاوضة في ضمان العمل واقتضاء البدل ؛ كذا في الهداية. وإنما قيد جريانه مجرى المفاوضة بهذين السببين لأن فيما عدا ذلك لم يجر هذا العقد مجرى المفاوضة حتى قالوا : إذا أقر أحدهما بدين من ثمن صابون أو أشنان مستهلك أو أجر أجير أو أجرة بيت لمدة مضت لم يصدق على صاحبه إلا ببينة ويلزمه خاصة لأن التنصيص على المفاوضة لم يوجد ونفاذ الإقرار موجب من أحدهما يبيع الشركة أن يجلس آخر على دكانه فيطرح عليه العمل بالنصف والقياس أن لا تجوز لأن . العمل ومن الآخر الحانوت واستحسن جوازها لأن التقبل من صاحب الحانوت عمل. قوله : (ولا تجوز شركة الدلالين) لأن عمل الدلالة لا يمكن استحقاقه بعقد الإجارة حتى لو استأجر دلالاً . له أو يشتري فالإجارة فاسدة إذا لم يبين له أجلاً كما صرح به في إجارة المجتبى. قوله : (والمعازي بالزمزمة) قال في القاموس : العزا الصبر أو حسنه كالتعزوة، والزمزمة الصوت البعيد له صوت الرعد، والمراد القراءة في المأتم الذي يصنع للأموات مع التمطيط قال ابن الشحنة في شرح دوي وتتابع
A trust and acceptance: if two tailors or a tailor and a dyer partner on the condition that they both accept work and the earnings are between them... And he died without clarifying with whom he deposited, there is no liability on him. The third: the judge if he took the orphan's wealth and deposited it with someone else and died without clarifying with whom he deposited, there is no liability on him. As for one of the two partners in a full partnership (mufawada), if the wealth was with him and he did not clarify the state of the wealth that was with him; some jurists mentioned that he is not liable and referred it to the original partnership, and that is a mistake. Rather, the correct view is that he is liable for his partner's share; thus in Fatawa Qadikhan from the book of Waqf. And by this it becomes clear that what is in Fath al-Qadir and some fatwas is weak, and that the partner is liable upon death due to ignorance, whether the partnership is 'inan or mufawada. His statement: (and acceptance, if two tailors or a tailor and a dyer partner on the condition that they accept work and the earnings are between them) with a damma (raising) as an 'atf on 'mufawada', is an explanation of the partnership of craftsmen. Its apparent meaning is that acceptance and work are other than mufawada and 'inan, but we have previously mentioned the contrary. In al-Bazzaziyya: the partnership of acceptance and work may be mufawada or 'inan; 'inan is what is in a specific trade, and mufawada is what is in all trades. End. And the benefit of it being mufawada will come later. This type of partnership is permitted because the goal is acquisition, and that is possible through agency, because he is an agent in half and a principal in half, so partnership is realized in the acquired wealth. And his statement 'or a tailor and a dyer' indicates that unity of work is not required. They said: unity of place is also not required, because the reason that permits it, which we mentioned, does not vary. So the meaning of his statement 'if two tailors partner' is two craftsmen, even if by legal construction (hukman), whether their work is the same or different, provided it is permissible work that can be legally claimed. This includes if two teachers partner for teaching children and instructing in writing and Quran, for the chosen view is its permissibility as in al-Bazzaziyya; and if one has a laundry tool and the other has a house, they partner to work in this house on condition that earnings are between them, it is permissible. Similarly for all crafts. And if one has the laundry tool and the other does the work, it is invalid, the profit is for the worker, and he owes the owner of the tool its rental equivalent; thus in al-Bazzaziyya. In al-Qunyah: three porters partnered on condition that one fills the sack, the second closes its mouth, and the third loads it and carries it to the client's house, with the wage divided equally among them; this partnership is invalid. Radi Allahu anhu said: its invalidity is due to these conditions, for the partnership of porters is valid if they partner in accepting work and doing it all together. And if they partner in accepting the books of pilgrims on condition that whatever Allah provides them with, it is half and half, this partnership is valid. End. And we said: even if it is by legal construction (hukman) to include the case where they partner in a craft and one of them is not proficient, it is valid, as will come. And we restricted it to permissible work because of what al-Bayri said in his marginalia on al-Ashbah regarding deposit. His statement: (Radi Allahu anhu said: its invalidity is due to these conditions). Al-Ramli said: It was previously stated that it does not become invalid due to invalid conditions. In al-Bazzaziyya: the partnership is nullified by some invalid conditions; so if they stipulate preference in loss, the partnership is not nullified, and it is nullified by stipulating a specific amount for one of them, and the apparent view is that it is not nullified by most conditions. End. And with this the answer can be obtained, contemplate. His statement: (And we said: even if it is by legal construction to include etc.) Al-Nahr said: There is no need for it, since what is shared is the work, not specifically tailoring. That is why they said: some forms of this... between them, and whatever work one of them accepts binds both, and the earnings of one of them is between them, and its existence if they partner without capital. In al-Bazzaziyya: if they partner in forbidden work, it is not valid. End. And we restricted it to being legally claimable because of what is in al-Qunyah: partnership of brokers in their work is not permissible, nor partnership of reciters in recitation with humming in the gathering because it is not claimable against them, nor partnership of beggars because agency in begging is not valid. And because of what is in al-Zahiriyya: if three reciters partner in a gathering and funeral gatherings with humming and melodies, this partnership is invalid because what they partnered for is not claimable against them or any one of them. End. And his statement 'on condition that they accept work' is not a restriction, because if they partner on condition that one of them accepts the goods and the other works, or one accepts the goods and cuts it then gives it to the other for sewing in halves, it is permissible, thus in al-Qunyah. But if the condition is that he only works and he accepts the job, it is permissible; if the condition is that the craftsman does not accept and only does the work, it is not permissible, because when silent, proving it by implication is established, and that is not possible with negation; thus in al-Muhit. And his statement 'and earnings are between them' includes if they stipulate equality or if they stipulate more profit for one of them; it is explicitly stated in al-Bazzaziyya, with the reasoning that work is variable and one may be more skillful. If they stipulate more for the less skilled, there is disagreement. End. And the correct view is permissibility because profit is based on the guarantee of work, not its reality; thus in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Qamus: 'qabila' is accepted (as in nasara, sami'a, daraba), 'qabala' (verbal noun), and 'taqabbala' (n. rare), the noun is 'qibala' and 'taqabbala' (n. rare). End. 'Atlaqaha'? His statement: (And whatever one of them accepts binds both) means each of them is sued for the work and sued for the wage, and the payer is discharged by paying to him. He made it absolute, so it includes if it is mufawada, which is apparent, and if they explicitly state 'inan, and that is istihsan, and qiyas is otherwise because suretyship necessitates mufawada. The reason for istihsan is that this partnership necessitates guarantee; do you not see that whatever work each of them accepts is guaranteed on the other, and thus he deserves the wage due to the efficacy of his acceptance on him, so it runs like mufawada in the guarantee of work and claim of compensation; thus in al-Hidaya. And he only restricted its running like mufawada to these two reasons because otherwise this contract does not run like mufawada, so they said: if one of them acknowledges a debt for the price of soap or potash consumed, or hires a laborer, or pays rent for a house for a past period, he is not believed against his partner except with evidence, and it is binding on him alone, because explicit stipulation of mufawada is not present, and the efficacy of acknowledgement is binding… one of them sells, the partnership is that another sits in his shop and throws work on him in halves, and qiyas is that it is not permissible because… work and the other the shop, and istihsan permits it because acceptance from the shop owner is a work. His statement: (partnership of brokers is not permissible) because the work of brokerage cannot be legally claimed through a contract of hire; even if one hires a broker… for him or buys, the hire is invalid if he did not specify a time, as stated in Ijarah al-Mujtaba. His statement: (and funeral gatherings with humming) said in al-Qamus: 'aza' is patience or its beauty like ta'ziyah; 'zamzama' is a distant sound like thunder; what is meant is recitation in the funeral gathering made for the dead with prolonging.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the partnership of craftsmen (شركة الصنائع) from Kanz al-Daqaiq. It begins by discussing a trust (amana) and acceptance (taqabbul) scenario: if two tailors or a tailor and a dyer partner on condition they both accept work and share earnings, the commentary explains the legal implications. First, it addresses liability when a partner dies without specifying the location of a deposit. Three cases are given: (1) a person who dies without clarifying the deposit – no liability? The text seems corrupt but suggests no liability; (2) a judge who takes an orphan's wealth and deposits it with another, then dies without clarifying – no liability; (3) a partner in a full partnership (مفاوضة) who had the wealth and died without clarifying – the correct view is he is liable for his partner's share, contrary to some jurists. This is supported by Fatawa Qadikhan, and it indicates that the partner's guarantee applies upon death due to ignorance, whether the partnership is 'inan or mufawada.

Then the commentary focuses on the matn phrase 'وتقبل إن اشترك خياطان...'. It explains that the phrase 'بينهما' is in the accusative (رفع) as an 'atf on 'مفاوضة'? Actually the commentary discusses the grammatical analysis. It states that partnership of acceptance and work (شركة التقبل والوجوه) can be either mufawada or 'inan, contrary to the apparent meaning of the matn. The benefit of it being mufawada will come later. This type of partnership is valid because the goal is acquisition, which is possible through mutual agency: each partner is an agent (وكيل) in half and a principal (أصيل) in half, so the acquired wealth becomes shared property.

The author then explains that unity of work (اتحاد العمل) is not required; thus a tailor and a dyer can partner. Similarly, unity of place is not required. What matters is that both are craftsmen (صانعان) even by legal construction (حكماً), i.e., if one is not actually a craftsman but is treated as such. The work must be halal and legally claimable (مستحق). Examples include teachers for children, or one providing a tool and the other a workshop. If one provides only a tool and the other does the work, the partnership is invalid (فاسد), and the worker gets the profit but must pay hire for the tool.

The commentary then gives an example from al-Qunyah: three porters decide that one fills the sack, the second closes it, and the third carries it – this partnership is invalid due to the specific conditions. However, if all porters together accept and do the work, it is valid. Another valid example is partners accepting pilgrims' books and sharing whatever Allah provides equally.

The author adds conditions: the work must be permissible; partnership in forbidden work is invalid. Also, the work must be legally claimable (مستحق), so partnership of brokers (دلالين) is invalid because brokerage cannot be enforced via hire contract if no time limit is set. Similarly, partnership of reciters who recite with humming (زمزمة) in funeral gatherings is invalid because such recitation is not legally claimable against them or anyone.

The condition 'on condition that they accept the work' is not restrictive; variations like one accepting and the other doing the work, or one cutting and the other sewing, are valid if the condition is not prohibitive. However, if the condition specifically prevents the craftsman from accepting work and only does work, it is invalid because the implied agency (اقتضاء) cannot be negated.

Regarding profit sharing, it can be equal or unequal; the correct view is that unequal profit is permitted (الصحيح الجواز) because profit is tied to the guarantee of work (ضمان العمل), not the actual work done. This is from Fath al-Qadir.

The commentary then addresses the scope of 'وكل ما يتقبله أحدهما يلزمهما': each is sued for work and wage, and the client is discharged by paying to either partner. This applies whether the partnership is explicitly mufawada or 'inan, based on istihsan, because the partnership inherently includes guarantee (ضمان). For example, if one partner acknowledges a debt for consumed goods or hires without evidence, it is not binding on the other unless proven, because explicit mufawada was not stipulated.

Finally, it discusses issues like one selling and the other’s shop, and the permissibility via istihsan. Also, it reiterates that partnership of brokers and humming reciters is invalid.

Key Terms
يلزمهما (yalzamuhuma): It binds both; meaning each partner is legally responsible for the work accepted by the other.
ضمان (daman): Liability/guarantee; in this context, the beneficial guarantee that justifies profit sharing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a Hanafi 'inan partnership, partner A accepts a job. Which of the following is true?
A) Partner B is not liable because 'inan does not have mutual guarantee.
B) Partner B is liable only if A had explicit permission.
C) Partner B is liable because the partnership implies guarantee (istihsan).
D) Partner B is liable only if the partnership is mufawada.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi partnership, even without explicit mufawada, each partner's acceptance of work binds the other due to the inherent guarantee of work, based on istihsan.

Ruling on Recitation with Tamteet and Melody
Ruling distinguishing two modes of recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between prohibited tamteet and recommended melodic recitation by applying the condition of non-distortion.

Core Idea
Tamteet that distorts the Qur'an is haram; beautiful melody without distortion is recommended.

Recitation of the Quran is an act of worship that can be performed in various styles. However, not all styles are equally permissible. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on two specific practices: excessive prolongation (tamteet) that alters the text, and melodious recitation (alhan). Understanding this distinction ensures that our recitation remains both beautiful and faithful to the divine words.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of recitation
First, identify the two modes mentioned: tamteet (excessive prolongation) and alhan (melodies). The passage gives a distinct ruling for each.
Tamteet is defined as prolongation that leads to adding or changing letters.
2
Recognize the decisive condition
The key condition is whether the recitation alters the letters or pronunciation. If it does, it falls under the prohibited tamteet. If it does not, it is melodious recitation.
The text says: 'if it is free from that' (i.e., from alteration).
3
Derive the ruling for each case
Apply the condition: tamteet with alteration is haram (prohibited); melody without alteration is mandub (recommended). The author strongly condemns the former and encourages the latter.
The ruling is conditional: the same style can be prohibited or recommended depending on its effect on the text.

الوهبانية : والمؤلف بالغ في النكير على إقرارهم على هذا في زمانه وعلى القراءة بالتمطيط ومنع جوازها وجواز سماعها، وقال بوجوب إنكارها وأطنب في إنكارها وذلك فيما إذا مطط تمطيطاً يؤدي إلى زيادة حرف ونحو ذلك، أما القراءة بالألحان إذا سلمت من ذلك فإنها مندوب إليها اهـ.
Al-Wahbaniyyah: The author was extreme in his criticism of their affirmation of this in his time and of recitation with tamteet (prolongation), and he prohibited its permissibility and the permissibility of listening to it, and he said it is obligatory to reject it, and he elaborated in its rejection – that is when he prolongs in a way that leads to adding a letter and the like. As for recitation with melodies (alhan) if it is free from that, then it is recommended (mandub ilayh).
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This short passage from al-Wahbaniyyah (a Hanafi work) provides a clear ruling on two types of recitation: (1) recitation with excessive prolongation (tamteet) that changes the letters or adds extra letters is absolutely prohibited (haram); the author strongly disapproves and says it must be rejected. (2) Recitation with melody (alhan) that does not distort the letters or pronunciation is recommended (mandub). This ruling is important for understanding the Hanafi position on tajweed and the permissibility of beautifying the recitation without violating the integrity of the Quranic text.

Key Terms
تمطيط (tamteet): Excessive prolongation of sounds in recitation that changes letters or adds sounds.
ألحان (alhan): Melodies or tunes used in recitation that do not alter pronunciation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on recitation with melody that does not add or change letters?
A) Haram
B) Makruh
C) Mandub (recommended)
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
Recitation with melody is recommended as long as it does not distort the Quranic text; distorting tamteet is strictly prohibited.
